Important News

Ministry of Finance Salt Tax Loan Contract 59

Hankou Correspondence: The salt tax loan of 3 million yuan, concluded between the Ministry of Finance and the banking community in Hankou, was established after Minister Song Ziwen visited Hankou on the 23rd of last month to negotiate its formation. Now, the full text of the contract is recorded below for readers' perusal:

[Contract between the Ministry of Finance of the National Government (hereinafter referred to as Party A) and the banks of Hankou (hereinafter referred to as Party B). Party A is seeking to borrow funds from Party B, and the two parties have agreed on the following terms: (1) The total loan amount is 3 million yuan, each bank’s obligation as shown below: Bank of China 500,000 yuan, Bank of Communications 400,000 yuan, Zhongnan Bank 170,000 yuan, Continental Bank 170,000 yuan, Jin Cheng Bank 170,000 yuan, Yanyeh Bank 170,000 yuan, Shanghai Bank 170,000 yuan, Sze Ming Bank 170,000 yuan, Zhejiang Xingye Bank 170,000 yuan, Zhejiang Industrial Bank 170,000 yuan, China Industrial Bank 80,000 yuan, Juxingcheng Bank 80,000 yuan, Guangdong Bank 80,000 yuan. Special Account 500,000 yuan. The above amounts will be transferred by the head offices to their respective Hankou branches. (2) The deadline for payment is seven installments from September 1, 1920. Each installment is paid every five days and averaged according to the total loan amount. Party A will instruct the Hubei Finance Commissioner's Office to collect and print receipts for each installment and hand them over to each bank for safekeeping. (3) The interest rate is calculated at 1.2% per month from the date of payment, regardless of the size of the construction. (4) Repayment and interest fund: 1. Except for the 80,000 yuan deducted from the monthly upper and middle ten-day periods (30,000 yuan each) and the lower ten-day period (20,000 yuan) from the Huai salt tax revenue on the Hubei bank for the repayment of foreign debts and the expenses of the salt affairs agency, all of the remaining tax revenues from the outer Hubei bank and the salt tax revenues from salt other than refined salt will be allocated until the principal and interest are paid off. The number of salt flower bills sold every five days shall be notified to Party B by the Hubei Bank Tax Transportation Bureau by letter. 2. Party A shall order the Hubei Bank Tax Transportation Bureau to instruct the Hankou Refined Salt Industry Association to repay 200,000 yuan per month from November of this year to 1 million yuan. Five separate cashier's checks totaling 200,000 yuan each shall be paid on December 5, 1920, January 5, February 5, March 5, and April 5 of 1920 and delivered to the bank receiving the money for safekeeping. The bank receiving the money shall issue a receipt for each installment, which shall be submitted to the Hubei Finance Commissioner's Office for examination and storage. (5) Party A shall use 3 million yuan of short-term customs treasury bills of 1919 as collateral and hand them over to each bank according to the amount of the loan. The principal and interest of the treasury bills upon maturity shall be collected directly by Party B and credited to Party A's account, and Party B shall issue a separate receipt and send it to the office organized by Party B for submission to the Hubei Finance Commissioner's Office for verification and storage. (6)

Method of repayment: 1. Party B shall designate the Hankou branch of the Bank of Communications as the bank to receive the money and organize an office of the Hubei Bank Salt Tax Loan Group, which shall send two special collectors to the tax collection office every day to collect all of the Huai salt taxes in full. Each installment shall be repaid every ten days, with interest reduced as the principal is repaid. The bank receiving the money is only responsible for safekeeping before the installment is repaid and does not recognize the return of interest. 2. When paying the regular and additional taxes for selling salt in Hubei Bank, the stamp of Party B's collector must be affixed to the tax payment receipt before the salt can be issued. The collector shall send all of the tax revenues to the bank receiving the money for deposit and safekeeping every day. 3. For salt sales in outer Hubei, the Tax Transportation Bureau shall, in conjunction with the Audit Office, instruct each sub-bureau to send all of the regular and additional taxes directly to the bank receiving the money for safekeeping. The temporary receipt shall be submitted to the Audit Office for transfer to the collector, who shall deposit it with the bank receiving the money for safekeeping. 4. Each bank of Party B shall issue a receipt for each installment repaid and submitted by the bank receiving the money to the Hubei Bank Salt Affairs Audit Office. After the principal and interest of this loan have been repaid, the receipts originally issued by Party B listed in Articles 4 and 5 shall be used to exchange the collateral and the receipts originally issued by Party A and cancel the contract. 5. If there are cashier's checks for the Huai salt additional taxes, the Audit Office shall affix its stamp on the back of the checks and send them to the bank receiving the money to obtain a receipt for safekeeping. After the checks have been collected upon maturity, the temporary receipt shall be used to collect the receipt and hand it over to the collector for deposit with the bank receiving the money. If the checks cannot be collected upon maturity, the bank receiving the money shall return them to the Audit Office for collection. (7) If there is any change in the salt tax system, regardless of the name or nature of the change, the fund for repayment of the principal and interest of the loan shall not be restricted and shall be fulfilled in accordance with the provisions of this contract. (8) Party A shall inform the Hubei Bank Tax Transportation Bureau of this loan contract and instruct the Audit General Office to instruct the Hubei Bank Audit Office to comply with it. In addition, the Tax Transportation Bureau and the Audit Office shall send a letter to Party B confirming their compliance. (9) Party A agrees not to use the Hubei Bank salt tax as collateral for other loans before the principal and interest of this loan have been repaid. (10) This contract is drawn up in five copies, with Party A and Party B each holding one copy as evidence, and the other three copies stored in the Hubei Finance Commissioner's Office, the Hubei Bank Tax Transportation Bureau, and the Hubei Bank Audit Office for reference. Borrowing Agency: Ministry of Finance, Song Ziwen, Borrowers: Various Banks, Special Account, Repayment Agencies: Hubei Bank Tax Transportation Bureau, Hubei Bank Audit Office, Auditors: Deputy Auditors, Witnesses: Hubei Finance Commissioner's Office, Ministry of Finance, August 25, 1919]

Promotion of Hunan Generals for Suppressing Bandits 60

Changsha Correspondence: The sacrifices in Hunan Province in the current suppression of bandits have been greater than before. Dai Douyuan, Deputy Division Commander and Commander of the 47th Brigade of the 16th Division; Tian Yingtang, Commander of the 93rd Regiment; and Wan Fangzhi, Commander of the 2nd Regiment of the 1st Brigade of the 31st Division, all died in battle. Chen Guangzhong, Commander of the 7th Independent Brigade; and Chen Wo, Commander of the 2nd Brigade of the 31st Division, were all reprimanded. The number of soldiers killed, wounded, and missing exceeded 2,000. As a result, Changsha, the provincial capital, was preserved, preventing the spread of bandit forces. When He Yingqin came to Hunan the other day, he summoned all the generals who had suppressed bandits to express his condolences and asked He Jian to promote and report the meritorious generals in this bandit suppression to the Commander-in-Chief for appointment in order to encourage them. On the verge of leaving, he explained that the Communist Party had been ordered by the Third International to attempt to seize the central commercial port of the three provinces of Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi in order to disrupt the Yangtze River as a base. Their goal was not limited to a corner of Hunan Province. The preservation of Changsha was sufficient to curb their ambitions, consolidate the upper reaches of the Yangtze River, and relieve the Party-State's worries about the south. He hoped that all levels of officers would embrace a spirit of great fearlessness, not be afraid of sacrifice, and strive for the foundation of the Party-State. The complete extermination of the Red bandits and the completion of great achievements would be the most glorious achievements for the Hunan military. All units that sacrificed in the suppression of bandits would be supplemented by one level according to the central regulations. For example, if a certain company sacrificed, the company would be replenished and promoted to a battalion. If a battalion sacrificed, it would be replenished and promoted to a regiment. If a regiment was replenished, it would be promoted to a brigade. If a brigade was replenished, it would be promoted to a division. A division could also be replenished and promoted to an army, and so on. After being encouraged by this, all the generals were united in their hatred of the enemy, and their morale was very high. However, because the fortification work near the provincial capital had not been fully completed, a large part of the troops could not be transferred to attack. The large army dispatched by the central government would not arrive in Jiangxi for a considerable period of time, and the friendly forces had not yet reached their designated locations. Therefore, for the time being, they would only firmly defend the fortresses to ensure safety, and judiciously dispatch troops to guard outside the positions. Who knew that the bandits such as Zhu Mao Huang Wu, etc., seeing that our army had not dispatched a large number of troops, took advantage of the heavy rain and wind on the night of the 10th and once again launched a fierce attack on the right-wing positions of Yuhuating, Amiling, and Southeast Du from the three directions of Dongshan Tiaoma Stream. After Liu Jianxu and Gong Bingfan's troops calmly responded to the attack, machine gunners, grenade squads, and broadsword teams were sent to meet them head-on. After holding out until 11:00 AM on the 11th, four aircraft from the air force dropped heavy bombs and bombed them, killing more than a thousand bandits and capturing hundreds. The bandits then collapsed in several directions towards the Dongshan Tiaoma Stream Tianxin Bridge area. Our army also pursued them out of the fortress to the Tianjiling Guitang Tongjingpu area, a distance of twenty miles, to guard. It is heard that the bandits are currently building fortifications in Dongshan Tiaoma Stream Yong'an Temple and other places to confront our army. However, the two groups of Peng Dehuai and Kong Hechong are retreating towards the Pingjiang Jinjing Gaoqiao area. Luo Lin's division is advancing in that direction to prevent Peng Bandit from having other plans. After this battle, it is expected that the bandits will not dare to try again lightly. As for the meritorious officers of all levels who should be promoted and rewarded in this bandit suppression, He Jian has already telegraphed Commander-in-Chief Jiang to request that a clear order be issued and the division be investigated as follows: (1) Wei Suzhong, Commander of the 15th Division, is transferred to the position of Senior Staff Officer of the Army, Navy, and Air Force Headquarters. Wang Dongyuan, Commander of the 43rd Brigade of the division, is promoted to Commander of the 15th Division. Yang Zhenpu, Commander of the regiment, is promoted to Commander of the 43rd Brigade. (2) Luo Fanying, Commander of the 16th Division, is transferred to the position of Senior Staff Officer of the Army, Navy, and Air Force Headquarters. Peng Weiren, Commander of the 46th Brigade of the division, is promoted to Commander of the 16th Division. Liu Jiren, Commander of the Regiment, is promoted to Commander of the 46th Brigade. Liu Yijing, Commander of the Regiment, is promoted to Commander of the 47th Brigade. Zhang Liangji is promoted to Commander of the 48th Brigade. (3) Liu Jianxu, Commander of the 19th Division, is promoted to Army Commander. Li Jue, Commander of the 57th Brigade of the division, is promoted to Commander of the 19th Division. Tao Liu, Commander of the Regiment, is promoted to Commander of the 57th Brigade. Deng Nanji, Commander of the Regiment, is promoted to Commander of the 56th Brigade. (4) Chen Guangzhong, Commander of the 7th Independent Brigade, is promoted to Division Commander. Wang Dezhang, He Yunqing, and Li Ang, Commanders of the Regiment, are promoted to Brigade Commanders. The number of Liu Jianxu's army and Chen Guangzhong's division will be determined after Commander-in-Chief Jiang promulgates them. As for the vacancies of regimental and battalion commanders, the army division commanders will select meritorious company commanders and forward them to the central government for appointment. (September 11)

Nanchang Municipal Government Reorganized According to New Municipal Law 61

Jiujiang Municipal Government Also Abolished

Nanchang Correspondence: According to the new municipal organization law promulgated by the National Government, municipal governments cannot be established in cities with a population of less than 230,000 and a total tax revenue of less than one-third of the city's total. Therefore, the Jiujiang municipal government has been abolished in accordance with the regulations. According to recent investigations, the population of Nanchang is over 230,000. In terms of tax revenue, according to the new law, the estimated annual land tax revenue is 210,000 yuan, the license tax is over 12,000 yuan, and the business tax is over 42,800 yuan. In addition, various other revenues total approximately 249,300 yuan per year, which accounts for more than one-half of the city's total revenue. Therefore, Mayor Xi Shizeng specifically reported the above situation to the higher authorities, and the municipal government was approved to continue to exist. However, due to the rampant bandits and communists in the province, the financial difficulties have reached their peak. The provincial government's subsidies and operating expenses to the municipal government are in arrears of approximately 400,000 yuan as of June of this year. Xi Shizeng is now reorganizing the municipal government in accordance with the newly promulgated municipal organization law. However, in order to save expenses, he has specifically submitted the following four items to the provincial government for approval: (1) The merger of the Bureau of Social Affairs and the Bureau of Land Affairs; (2) The fundraising for the operating expenses and subsidies for the establishment of autonomous districts and neighborhoods in the city; (3) According to the new municipal law, the governing body of the Public Security Bureau is the Police Department. This body has not yet been established. How should it be handled? (4) The police expenses account for the majority of the municipal government's expenditures. Since May of 1919, the police expenses were originally intended to be covered by the provincial treasury subsidy. Now the Finance Department owes the city a large amount of subsidies. It should be allocated immediately for disbursement or transferred to the provincial government for direct disbursement starting from 1920. After receiving the report, Chairman Lu of the Provincial Government submitted it to the 312th Provincial Affairs Conference, which decided to hand it over to Chen Jiadong, Zhang Feiran, Jiang Jilu, and Wang Yinxi for review and to formulate three measures, which were then submitted to the 313th Provincial Affairs Conference for approval. The measures are as follows: 1. Article 17 of the newly promulgated municipal organization law stipulates that if it is necessary to reduce the number of bureaus in the city, they may be changed to departments, except for the Public Security Bureau. It has been found that the organs were previously reduced due to financial difficulties in the province, and the fourth temporary public deliberation meeting decided on a method to do so. Now that the bandits and communists have not been cleared and the financial difficulties are severe, it is necessary to tighten the situation to meet the actual situation. It is proposed that the Land and Social Affairs Bureaus of the Nanchang Municipal Government be merged, and the Municipal Government shall establish an Education Department to manage the matters in Article 8, Item 10. The original Public Welfare Department of the Municipal Government shall be renamed the Department of Social Affairs and manage the matters in Article 8, Items 1 to 9. The matter in Article 8, Item 18, managed by the Land Bureau shall be considered and efforts shall be made to save money. Separate detailed staffing budgets shall be formulated and submitted to the Provincial Government for approval and implementation. 2. The subsidy for districts and neighborhoods should be properly raised by the municipal government within the urban area. The investigation and operating expenses for prior preparations should be carefully investigated and planned by the municipal government, and detailed budgets should be formulated before the Finance Department or the Budget Committee is instructed to review them. 3. The new municipal organization law stipulates that cities where the provincial government is located shall not establish a Public Security Bureau. The matters managed by the Public Security Bureau shall be managed by the provincial police agency. It has been found that there is currently no police agency in the provincial capital, and how to organize this agency has not been officially announced. It is proposed that the Nanchang Municipal Public Security Bureau be temporarily changed to the Jiangxi Provincial Public Security Bureau and directly under the jurisdiction of the Provincial Government. All internal organization and required expenses of the bureau shall still be spent according to the original plan and approved budget. After the organization of the provincial police agency is officially announced, it will be corrected in accordance with the regulations.

As for the abolition of the Jiujiang Municipal Government, the Department of Civil Affairs also convened various public organizations in Jiujiang to formulate post-abolition measures: (1) The administrative expenses of 4,200 yuan subsidized to the city shall be requested to be exempted by the provincial government; (2) The operating expenses shall be reported and paid for actual expenses; (3) The Jiujiang Municipal Public Security Bureau shall be changed to the Jiujiang County Public Security Bureau; (4) The Jiujiang Municipal Works Bureau shall be merged into the Jiujiang County Construction Bureau; (5) The Jiujiang Municipal Finance Bureau shall be merged into the County Finance Bureau; (6) The Lushan Administration Bureau shall be directly under the jurisdiction of the Provincial Government; (7) The disbanded personnel of the municipal government shall be paid one month's salary (September 12).

###韓復榘部搜剿膠東股匪

Jinan Correspondence: Shandong’s customs are strong and fierce, known for producing bandits. Since the Xinhai Revolution, bandits have been especially numerous. In the Yan Prefecture of southern Shandong, the Cao Prefecture of western Shandong, and the Jiaodong area, there has hardly been a year or month without banditry.

Page 10

The bandit disasters, coupled with continuous warfare, have led many shrewd bandit leaders to seize the opportunity to move and appease others, thereby expanding their strength. Consequently, banditry inevitably follows every military campaign. Observing the bandit situation over the years, the bandits in southern and western Shandong are fiercer than those in Jiaodong, but not as deeply rooted. Jiaodong bandits, whenever there is a military campaign, take advantage of the military's lack of preparation to create disturbances, or borrow military flags to ravage the area. When the military situation is stabilized, they disperse as civilians. Their firearms are mostly hidden deeply; those that are not hidden are used to join local defense groups, using a half-bandit, half-gentry status as protection. Therefore, although the noise of banditry in Jiaodong in recent years has not been as loud as in southern and western Shandong, the accumulated banditry is even deeper. After the recent Shandong war, western Shandong, influenced by western Henan, saw various bandit gangs raising military flags, making it difficult to distinguish between soldiers and bandits. In southern Shandong, Sun Meisong gathered a division in Yixian County last month and formed it into a regular army, which was sent to Haizhou for training, freeing the area from banditry. However, in the eastern Shandong area, because the Central Army and the Jin Army were about to engage in a major battle on the Jiaoji Railway for nearly two months, the bandit troops recruited by the Jin side in Shandong were mostly stationed in Zhoucun, Boxing, Qingzhou, and Huantai. After the Jin Army was defeated, the bandits hid in the area and committed disturbances. After Han Fuju, the commander-in-chief of the First Army Corps, came to Jinan with his troops, he ordered Cao Fulin, the commander of the Fourteenth Army, and Zhan Shuyi, the commander of the Fifty-eighth Brigade and concurrently the commander of bandit suppression in Jiaodong, to separately search and suppress bandits in various parts of eastern Shandong, and sent Li Shuchun, the chief staff officer of the First Army Corps, to supervise the suppression. In recent days, Army Commander Cao Fulin and Deputy Army Commander Xu Wenyao have led their Zhao Xinde Brigade and Rong Guangxing Brigade to separately search and suppress bandits in Huantai, Guangrao, Qingzhou, and Boxing. All bandit gangs such as Zhou Liu, Mi San, Shi Fengming, Wang Shaozhou, Zhang Erlaohu, Cai Guanjun, Caoshangfei, and Diantoutou have been completely defeated. The fierce bandit Cui Zhenlong gang in Guangrao was also exterminated on the seventh of this month. That night, Section Chief Xie Bang of the staff office of the First Army Corps received telegrams from Xu Wenyao and Li Shuchun reporting the details of the bandit suppression. On the eighth, Li Shuchun brought more than a hundred captured bandits from Xindian to Jinan to report to Han Fuju on the bandit suppression process and defense situation. The telegram from Xu Wenyao is recorded as follows: [Urgent to Jinan, Staff Office of the First Army Corps, Brother Xie Bang, Jiaodong fierce bandit Cui Zhenlong (aka Cui Jiu) occupied more than ten villages including Zhao Aizhuang, Xiao Zhang, and Zhang Zhao west of Guangrao for more than twenty years, levying grain, extorting money, looting, burning, and killing without restraint. The reason why this bandit was able to prolong his life for so long was that he took advantage of the changing situation and bribed various parties. The front-line troops in battle were unwilling to deal with him, so his power gradually grew, building walls and fortresses, resembling an emperor of the soil. This time, our brothers led the Zhao and Rong Brigades to successively suppress more than ten large and small bandit gangs such as Zhou Liu, Mi San, Shi Fengming, Wang Shaozhou, Zhang Erlaohu, Cai Guanjun, Caoshangfei, and Diantoutou. Cui became frightened and used his old trick of begging to be incorporated into the army. We were in Guangrao at the time, and because our Rong Brigade was suppressing bandits in Boxing, we could not take care of it, so we pretended to agree and temporarily ordered them to stand by in place. On the fourth, all troops had been mobilized and ordered the Rong Brigade to depart from Boxing at dawn and advance towards the area north of the bandit fortress. The Zhao Brigade, via Liyuanzi and Cheng Bingzhuang, advanced towards the area south of the bandit fortress. At ten o'clock in the morning, our Rong Brigade had eliminated the bandits of Zhang Xiahou in Xingfu Town, and the remaining bandits all fled into the Zhao and Ai Erzhuang fortresses and stubbornly resisted. At the same time, our Zhao Brigade also occupied Xiao Zhang. By twelve o'clock noon, the bandit fortress had been surrounded. We concentrated more than ten light and heavy mortars and mountain guns to bombard the bandit fortress fiercely. The bandits suffered heavy casualties. Cui personally led the cavalry to charge out several times but were repulsed. Seeing the fire starting in the fortress, the bandits were even more frightened and eagerly wanted to flee, but they were surrounded on all sides by our army and could not succeed. Then, because it was difficult to attack at night, at dawn on the sixth, we used artillery fire to force the bandits to desperately break out from the southwest gates. The Rong and Zhao Brigades intercepted them head-on, and the bandits suffered more than half casualties. Cui led the remnants of more than two hundred men out of the north gate, detouring towards the Tieshan area. Our army tracked and pursued them. At five o'clock in the afternoon, the bandits fled to Que Mountain Station and were resting. Our Zhao Brigade rushed to the scene and launched a sudden attack on the unprepared bandits, who abandoned their weapons and scattered. Coincidentally, our Rong Brigade also arrived and intercepted them on all sides. Corpses were everywhere. It has not yet been investigated whether Cui was among them. The fierce bandits who had occupied Jiaodong for more than twenty years have now been completely suppressed. In this battle, more than three hundred bandits were killed and more than one hundred were captured alive, seizing more than two hundred guns, dozens of portable guns, more than one hundred mules and horses, and more than thirty thousand rounds of various bullets. Especially reported by Xu Wenyao and Li Shuchun.] (September 9th)

Su Provincial Department of Agriculture's Opinion on Establishing a Rice Market in the Capital 62

The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Agriculture previously received an order from the Provincial Government to assist in the case reported by the Nanjing Municipal Government regarding the preparation of a rice market, in accordance with the Executive Yuan's order. It was instructed to conduct a detailed review and report back. After review, the department submitted a report to the Provincial Government, stating: [The Fifth 019 Order of the Government instructs that, in accordance with the Executive Yuan's order, the Nanjing Municipal Government reported on the preparation of a rice market and requested assistance in a detailed review and report back, etc., and copies of the regulations and proposals were issued. Upon investigation, the establishment of a rice market in the capital has both advantages and disadvantages. In terms of advantages, after the establishment of a rice market in the capital, rice and grain from the upper reaches of the Yangtze River will inevitably gather in the capital and be distributed to various places. The sources and destinations will be clear, and the price of rice can be expected to be stable and not monopolized by a few unscrupulous merchants, and the malpractice of hoarding and speculation can also be avoided. This is one advantage. The establishment of a rice market in the capital will ensure that various miscellaneous grains will be sold smoothly along with rice and grain, and the economy of farmers in Jiangsu Province can be presented with a vibrant image. This is the second advantage. As for the disadvantages, Jiangsu Province has been implementing rice bans due to frequent disasters. If a rice market is established in the capital, this rice ban will inevitably be completely lifted, not only inconsistent with previous regulations, but also easily causing misunderstandings among the people. This is one disadvantage. Also, assuming that the rice-producing areas in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River, such as Anhui, Jiangxi, Hubei, Hunan, and Sichuan, implement rice bans or encounter poor harvests and rice and grain disappear, the capital's rice market will be empty. It will not only absorb rice and grain from Jiangsu Province, but also have a significant impact on the food supply of Jiangsu Province. This is the second disadvantage. Therefore, in the humble opinion of the department, the capital should have two prerequisites for establishing a rice market: (1) Prohibit the export of rice and grain from the country and open up domestic rice bans. The Customs is currently not prohibiting the export of rice and grain, so that at a time of national food panic, the export of rice is still happening daily, which is not a blessing for the people's livelihood. In the future, the Ministry of Finance should order customs offices in various places to strictly prohibit it. On the one hand, in order to prevent the capital's rice market from being empty and affecting the food supply in Jiangsu Province, the central government should issue an order to all provinces to open up domestic rice bans, and rice and grain should be allowed to circulate freely between provinces for regulation. Moreover, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hubei, Hunan, and Sichuan are the most abundant rice-producing areas in our country. The prosperity and decline of farmers' economic conditions depend entirely on whether agricultural products can be sold smoothly. If each province restricts the purchase of grain by itself, low grain prices will harm farmers, which is also not appropriate. Therefore, opening up domestic rice bans can not only relieve the emptiness of the capital's rice market, but also increase the economic capacity of farmers nationwide. (2) The capital's rice market should be organized and managed by a central agency with the aim of regulating the people's food supply, not just limited to the relief of hundreds of thousands of citizens in the capital. Before receiving orders, the reasons were gathered and the opinions were drafted and submitted to the government for review.]

Jiangsu Provincial Capital to Build Two Main Roads 63

Zhenjiang Flag Station to be Expanded

The Jiangsu provincial capital originally planned to build Zhongshan and Zhongzheng two main roads, as well as Jinshan Road and Boxian Road. Jinshan Road, from the station to Jinshan, was completed by the end of July. Boxian Road has not yet been built. Zhongshan Road starts from the Grand Railway Station in the west-north-east direction to the old North Gate. Zhongzheng Road starts from the South Gate Station (i.e., the Flag Station) in the south-north direction to Gaobeiqiao (planned to open a new North Gate). The intersection point is in the Dashikou east of the provincial government. It was originally planned to complete the third section of Zhongshan Road from Zhugan Lane to the North Gate and the first section of Zhongzheng Road from the Flag Station to Dashikou before the Double Tenth Festival. The Flag Station has only a single track in front of the station outside the South Gate. Only local trains and third and fourth class cars stop there, while the remaining express trains generally do not stop. This time, the starting point of Zhongzheng Road is at this station. After the road is open, the journey to the provincial government will be one-third shorter than the road from the Grand Railway Station. The provincial government had previously consulted the Railway Department to expand the South Gate Station and ordered all express trains to stop for passengers. Now the Jinghu Railway Bureau has received an order from the Railway Department to implement stops for all express trains, Beijing-Hangzhou intermodal express trains, and night express trains from September 15th. However, Zhongshan Road, one of the two main roads of the provincial capital, can barely be completed on the Double Tenth Festival, while the wooden bridge ditch of Zhongzheng Road has just been completed recently. The road surface still requires 20,000 yuan, which cannot be allocated. Although it is a dirt road, it has not been rolled flat by a road roller, and even rickshaws cannot travel. Although express trains will stop, it is still inconvenient to enter the city.

After Singapore Restricted Chinese Laborers 64

The Impact on Chaoshan

More than 8,000 People Waiting for Ships

Shantou Correspondence: The Singapore government implemented restrictions on the entry of Chinese laborers on September 1st. At the end of last month, the Haitong ship had already carried back more than four hundred excess passengers. Many others from distant places who are unaware of the situation are still waiting for ships in Shantou. It is estimated that on average, more than 10,000 people go to Singapore from Shantou every month. Now, under strict restrictions, the six ships of Taikoo Foreign Company, Anqing and Andong, etc., are limited to carrying 1,715 people per month. The two ships of the Zhahua Company, Jinma and Wanfusi, are limited to 850 people per month. The three ships of the Hefeng Company, Fengqing, Fengping, and Fenghua, are limited to 810 people per month. The two ships of the Boning Company, Haixing and Xialishi, are limited to 280 people per month. It is estimated that the number of people going abroad from Shantou Port has been reduced from more than 10,000 to more than 3,600. There are currently more than 8,000 passengers waiting for ships, but those who travel in first or second class cabins and those who have passports are not subject to this restriction. Therefore, the Shantou Municipal Government had previously issued 300 passports from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, which were exhausted in less than ten days. However, the procedures for obtaining a passport are extremely troublesome. Those who go abroad must submit a request to the Municipal Government. After the Municipal Government approves it, they must also have a store guarantee and be interviewed by the head of the Municipal Government before being allowed to issue it. On the 4th, the Shantou Travel Industry Association specially sent Wang Daofu and others as representatives to the Municipal Government to request improvements in the passport application procedures. Also, the boat ticket from Shantou to Singapore was 28 yuan each. After September 1st, the price was increased to 36 yuan. Ordinary passengers cannot buy tickets directly from foreign companies. The number of tickets is controlled by the inns of the Travel Industry Association. Inns have recently taken the opportunity to raise prices, selling each ticket for 45 yuan. The inns opened by the Meixian Dabu gang sell each ticket for 56 yuan. They said that they cannot maintain their business without doing so. Although the ticket price is high, the shipping companies are also complaining incessantly and have been increasing cargo capacity in recent days to make up for the losses. According to shipping companies, the Singapore government has set a time limit of three months, so they have no choice but to endure and maintain the status quo. If this regulation continues to be effective after November, the shipping companies will inevitably not sit idly by and will only have to divert ships to other ports. The Fenghua of the Hetong Company and the Haixing of the Boning Company have already sailed to other places. (September 5th)

Crisis for Chinese Laborers in Nanyang is Increasingly Urgent 65

Siam Follows British Colonies in Restricting Foreigners' Entry

Dutch Colonies Increase Entry Tax by 150 Guilders

Malay and Indian Laborers Usurping the Position of Chinese Laborers

Nanyang Special Dispatch: The Nanyang Islands are located in the tropics, where summer-like greenery persists year-round. But who is responsible for today's prosperity? The most famous industries in Nanyang are rubber and tin. Who is it that collects drops of latex and smelts lumps of tin ore into commodities that are sold worldwide? Let us try to analyze the development history of the Nanyang Islands to find the reasons for their prosperity. Although there are many, the hardworking Chinese laborers have made a considerable contribution. The number of Chinese laborers living in various ports in Nanyang is the largest (approximately 2.3 million in the Malay Peninsula). During the European War, Chinese laborers occupied the most important position in Nanyang. It was the Chinese laborers who maintained the Nanyang industries from closing down. It was also the Chinese laborers who reclaimed wasteland and built roads. After the European War, as the prices of rubber and tin rose daily, Chinese laborers took advantage of their spirit of hard work and struggle to obtain a superior economic position. Taking rubber workers as an example, they can earn an average of three yuan per day (rubber cutting workers are paid according to the number of catties, the more they cut, the more they earn). There has been a reason why the country has regarded Nanyang as a source of wealth. In addition, the motherland has been plagued by natural and man-made disasters in recent years, social order has not been stable, and the level of life has been increasing day by day. Therefore, those who leave their hometowns and go abroad to Nanyang come shoulder to shoulder, thinking that if they go to the South Island, even if they cannot return home full of money, they will still have enough to wear and eat. Who knows that the crisis for Chinese laborers in Nanyang has been secretly spread around them? This is not a reporter's alarmist talk, but there are facts to show us: (1) The Malay Peninsula restricts the import of Chinese laborers. (2) Siam promulgated immigration regulations. (3) The Dutch East Indies increased import taxes. The three are described in detail as follows:

Since the price of rubber and tin has plummeted, the fear of unemployment has spread throughout the South Island. Sir Cecil Clementi, Governor of Malaya, announced on August 1st that the import of Chinese laborers would be restricted for three months. During the months of August, September, and October, only 5,000 Chinese immigrants per month were allowed to land in Singapore, and the quota was allocated to various shipping companies. If there is an excess, they will be ordered to be transported back to China. According to the regulations of the Straits Settlements government in Malaya, any decree issued by the Governor must be approved by the Legislative Council. If the restriction on the import of Chinese laborers is not passed by the Legislative Council, it can only be implemented for one month (this is the Governor's special power). Now, on August 25, the Legislative Council has passed this case, so the restriction on the import of Chinese laborers can undoubtedly be implemented for three months. It is still difficult to predict whether it will be extended when it expires. However, this regulation does not restrict the import of women. The reason is that [the gender ratio of imported Chinese can be improved slightly]. Seeing this, the number of Chinese laborers coming to Malaya in the future has been reduced by two-thirds. (According to statistics from the seven states of Malaya, a total of 17,383 Chinese immigrants entered in July of this year. Since the news of the restriction on Chinese laborers was transmitted to the motherland, the price of passenger tickets to Xiamen and Shantou has reportedly increased from more than ten yuan to forty yuan, and some have increased to forty-eight yuan in Shantou. Moreover, there are many passengers and no tickets, and they are competing to buy them, which shows the great impact on the people's livelihood in Fujian and Guangdong.)

Amidst the restrictions on the import of Chinese laborers in Malaya, the Siamese government also announced immigration laws restricting the entry of foreigners. The immigration laws promulgated by Siam consist of ten articles (as seen in previous reports). Siam and our country have not mutually sent ministers. Previously, Chinese compatriots entering Siam had to pay a body fee of 15 sen per person, which is approximately 20 yuan in national currency. This time, the immigration laws promulgated by Siam were translated by the Japanese Minister to Siam and forwarded to our country. Therefore, whether overseas Chinese can enter the country in accordance with the provisions of the regulations is what our government's Ministry of Foreign Affairs hopes to discuss good methods to resolve the doubts of overseas Chinese.

The government of the Dutch East Indies colonial territory decided to increase taxes to compensate for the lack of entry and exit budget for next year. The most relevant to overseas Chinese is that from 1931, the import tax (dock tax) per person will be increased from 100 guilders to 150 guilders, and the commercial stamp tax will be doubled compared to the old rules. Since the distribution last month, the general chambers of commerce in Medan and Bacheng, regardless of Chinese, Malay, or Indian, have petitioned to reduce the stamp tax, which may be reduced, but the dock tax cannot be reduced. The most bizarre thing is that contracted laborers entering the country (that is, what our country calls "piglets") must also pay half of the dock tax, which is 75 guilders. Contracted laborers were originally a private trafficking of people, which was most prevalent in Fujian and Guangdong provinces a few years ago and has now been slightly reduced. According to old regulations, contracted laborers entering Dutch territory did not pay the dock tax, but only paid a stamp tax of one and a half guilders at the end of the contract period (during the contract period, there is work but no wages) to obtain a residence permit and be allowed to live freely in Dutch territory. According to the newly promulgated regulations, Chinese laborers whose contract has expired must pay a landing tax of 75 guilders before being allowed to reside. The increase in taxes for contracted laborers is so huge that it has caused major debates in the Dutch Indian National Assembly, but there is no concrete solution. Therefore, the increase in the dock tax is inevitable, as it has been included in the next year's entry budget. However, Chinese laborers entering Dutch territory, if they enter freely, should pay a dock tax of 150 guilders from next year. If they are contracted laborers, they should pay a dock tax of 75 guilders, which is inevitable.

Overall, the current crisis for Chinese laborers in Nanyang is like this, and the future difficulties are like that. The superior position in the past may be cut off by this. Moreover, in recent years, Indian and Malay laborers have been competing with Chinese laborers for jobs more and more fiercely. Malay and Indian people think it is a great opportunity because their lives are simple and they have wages of two to three cents per day. Chinese laborers win by their working skills, and their work efficiency cannot be reached by Indian and Malay laborers. However, wages are too high, and they must have at least five cents per day to survive. Therefore, all mechanical work such as rubber cutting and tin mining in various gardens and mines has mostly abandoned expensive Chinese laborers and hired Indian and Malay laborers. Chinese laborers in Nanyang are rarely able to endure hardships, and most of them only care about the present and waste money recklessly. They already lack private savings, and they are far behind the Japanese, who can be diligent and thrifty, reclaim wasteland and build bridges, and accumulate huge sums of money in less than ten years before returning home. Once they lose their jobs and buy boats to return home, they still rely on friends to help them, which is common. Therefore, since the business market has been cold and unemployment has increased sharply, the wandering and helpless Chinese laborers have caused infinite pain. Singapore and Penang have sent old and weak Chinese laborers back to China, totaling more than 3,000 people. This is just a drop in the bucket. There are still many people who live in the open air and have nowhere to live. If this continues, unemployed Chinese laborers will never have a way out and can only hope to return home. Japan and the Americas have already expelled Chinese laborers from their countries. Chinese laborers in Nanyang have also returned to their countries due to the fear of unemployment, only to make the number of unemployed in the country more rampant. The people's livelihood and the national economy are concerned, which is not light. What will people with good intentions do to deal with the aftermath? I really hope for it. (August 25th, Little Gray)

Kunshan 66

Fan Youcheng Escorted Back to Kunshan: Fan Youcheng, a worker at Ye Qiyuan's winery outside the West Gate of Kunshan, had previously had a quarrel with a buyer named Xiao Zhou and suddenly beat Xiao Zhou to death before fleeing without a trace. The county government verified that the incident was true and strictly pursued the case. It is now known that Jiang Guilin, the manager of the winery, dispatched friends to search in all directions after the murderer escaped. They found Fan in Baimao, Changshu County, and handed him over to the local Public Security Bureau, who escorted him to the Changshu County Government for temporary detention. After reporting this to Magistrate Pang, he prepared a document and dispatched police to escort Fan Youcheng back to Kunshan at 3 PM on the 12th. After a brief interrogation by the trial officer, Chen, the suspect denied everything and was immediately detained to await interrogation.

Suzhou 67

Major Robbery Case in Wujiang: More than ten robbers suddenly arrived at Nanma Village, Wujiang County, on the night of the 10th and robbed various shops. The following was robbed: Yuantai Xiang's dry goods store: 12 silver dollars, 270 small silver coins, 81,000 copper coins, and 3 qian of gold jewelry. Ni Yuanxing's tofu shop: 10 silver dollars. Tianshengtang drug store: 161 silver dollars, 184 small silver coins, 53,000 copper coins, 3 gold rings, 1 gold watch, 1 pearl flower, 1 pair of pearl rings, 3 gold buttons, and 1 gold heart totaling 9 qian, and 1 inlaid treasure ring, and 1 pair of gold rings. Si'er store: 390 paper dollars, 196 small silver coins, 80,000 copper coins. Risheng Xiang: 25 silver dollars, 54 small silver coins. Gongchangcheng: 15 silver dollars, 94 small silver coins. Yuhe's house: 1 gold ring, 66 paper dollars, and 36 small silver coins. Chenglongxing: 24 paper dollars, 120 small silver coins, 30,000 copper coins, and 2 gold rings. Niu Yuanshun: 50 silver dollars and 1 gold ring. In addition to the above twelve shops, more than 200 pieces of clothing were lost. After the robbers left, the victims reported the case to the commander of the third squad of the 15th Public Security Team stationed in Fanshui, Lu Wuben, who requested an arrest warrant and reported the case to the third district of the Public Security Bureau in this area for verification.

Party and Government Joint Trial of Reactionary Case: Since the 97th Anniversary, the Public Security Bureau has successively arrested twenty-one people suspected of being reactionary, including Song, Song Linhheshang, Song Zhaocai, Kong Shaoxi, Wu Jinli, Wang Yutian, Hu Zhiji, Wang Zhangxian, Gu Chaoyan, Song Yucheng, Li Hong, Chen Ping, Pan Agen, Dai Amao, Pan Afu, Zhou Akun, Pan Qingbao, Liu Arong, Yao Xuan, Wang Pansheng, and Huang Chuntao. After a brief interrogation by Zhang, the director of the Judicial Section, it was determined that ten people, including Wu Jinli, Wang Yutian, Wang Zhangxian, Gu Chaoyan, Song Yucheng, Pan Agen, Dai Amao, Pan Afu, Zhou Akun, and Pan Qingbao, were unlikely to be suspects and were released on bail the day before. The remaining eleven people, including Song Qin and Yao Xuyan, are still being temporarily detained at the Public Security Bureau. At 10 PM the night before (the 12th), Director Zou, the county party committee member, and others jointly interrogated them and submitted the case to the provincial government for instructions.

Interesting News About the Arrest of the Regiment Commander: On the afternoon of the day before yesterday, the Wu County Party Department suddenly received a person holding a commission from the Third Regiment of the Central Army for the Suppression of Rebels, Xu Huaihai Guerrilla Headquarters, to deliver it to Bo Gonglei, the party committee member and organization minister. Because Committee Member Bo did not know the regiment commander Wang Zhenya and had not contacted him beforehand, he immediately interrogated the messenger, Mr. Fang. According to Mr. Fang, Regiment Commander Wang is currently living in the Xie family's home at No. 64 Zhongyouji Lane. Because Committee Member Bo had been searching for the Communist Party very strictly in Suzhou in recent days, he feared that the Communist Party might be disrupting things, so he immediately sent Mr. Fang and the original commission to the Second Branch of the County Public Security Bureau for investigation. The chief of the branch, Pan, immediately sent personnel to arrest Regiment Commander Wang. Wang had already left for Shanghai and was immediately tracked to the station. At around 9 PM, Wang was spotted trying to board a train on the station platform and was arrested and taken to the bureau. According to Wang, he is currently the commander of the Third Replenishment Regiment of the Xu Huaihai Guerrilla Headquarters and was commissioned as a councilor because he knew Bo. The situation was confusing for a while, and Wang was immediately escorted to the headquarters to be interrogated by the chief of the Judicial Section. According to Wang, he had been a monk in a temple in Wufunong and had dealings with Bo from time to time, but they had been separated for many years. After Committee Member Bo went to the bureau to identify him, Wang was immediately released, and the incident became a laughing stock.

Suzhou Gentry Organizes a Merchant Corps for Self-Defense: In order to supplement the local self-defense force, local gentry Zhang Zhongren and others initiated the organization of the Suzhou Merchant Corps for Self-Defense and submitted regulations to the county government for approval. The county government received an order from the provincial government yesterday that the provincial government meeting had approved the record.

The court pursued them but failed to catch them and sent telegrams to military and police agencies to arrest them.

Wuxi 70

The Director of the Finance Bureau was replaced yesterday. Chen Liangdong, the Director of the County Finance Bureau, recently resigned to the Provincial Finance Department due to his inability to raise various funds for the province and county. His resignation was approved, and Zhuang Yeguang was appointed to fill the vacancy in Wuxi. Chen was transferred to the Department to serve as an inspector. After receiving his appointment, Zhuang arrived in Wuxi from the province on the afternoon of the 12th and took over his duties at the Bureau at 9 a.m. on the 13th.

Two Sisters Drowned While Gathering Water Caltrop. Hui, a resident of Huijiali in the Eleventh District (Nanyan City) of the county, had two daughters. The elder, named Axiu, was 18 years old, and the younger, Jinmei, was 10 years old. Both were beautiful and had been betrothed. In the afternoon of the day before yesterday, at 4 p.m., Jinmei and Axiu rode together in a water caltrop basin to gather water caltrop in a nearby water caltrop field. Unexpectedly, while traveling halfway across the river, they accidentally capsized, and both fell into the river. They cried loudly for help. People who heard the news rushed to rescue them. Axiu was rescued before she drowned, but when Jinmei was pulled out, she had already drowned.

Autumn Cocoons Are Successively Weighed. The autumn sericulture season in the four rural districts of Wuxi has begun, and the main groups of silk workers have long since gone to work. Silk trading firms on the east and west roads have also successively opened their scales on the days before yesterday. A total of 95 silk trading firms have been reported to have opened for business, with a better supply of cocoons than last year. The Southern Spring, Shitou, Gongtai, and Chang silk trading firms quoted a price of 45 yuan per dan. The various firms in Zhouxin Town quoted prices ranging from 40 yuan to 45 yuan per dan. In the northern rural areas, such as Qianzhou and Yuqi, the silk trading firms quoted prices ranging from 50 yuan to 60 yuan per dan. In Tangtou, Shitou, and other places, the quoted price was 53.5 yuan per dan.

The Construction Committee Pays Attention to Electric Irrigation. In recent years, most of the farmland irrigation in Wuxi, Changzhou, and other counties has been done using water-lifting machines. Since the Construction Committee took over the Qishuyan Power Plant in Changzhou, villagers have mostly used electric power for irrigation, and the cost of farmland irrigation is lower than that of machine-operated water lifting. However, due to the lack of adequate equipment at the Qishuyan Power Plant in Wuxi, machine-operated water lifting is still used. Recently, the Construction Committee decided to build a large Gaoqiao power plant near Gaoqiao outside the North Gate of Wuxi. The plant's planning is currently underway, and construction is scheduled to begin within the year. In the future, after the large power plant is established, farmland irrigation and factories in various counties will be greatly facilitated.

Yixing Requests Suppression of Bandit Remnants in Taihu Lake. Since the Taihu Lake bandits were extensively suppressed by the government and police, they have dispersed and fled everywhere, causing disturbances. Recently, a group of lake bandits has been harassing various villages and towns along the lake in Yixing, looting everywhere. Sun Gongqi, the magistrate of Yixing County, telegraphed the Second Water Police District stationed in Wuxi yesterday, requesting that a warship be dispatched to patrol the lake along Yixing to clear out the remnants of the bandits. Mao Mujun, the chief of the Water Police District, immediately ordered the Baosu shallow-water warship to sail to various places along the lake in Yixing to patrol carefully.

The previous report did not clarify the supplementary statement, and it was fabricated that the missing ammunition was not due to the transfer. Who would believe it? The commander should be responsible for compensating for the missing ammunition and handing it over to the successor. Not a single missing round is allowed to prevent the recurrence of the incident with military supplies. The boat was damaged and the same thing as the box cannon was investigated.

Cai Rushan Arrested in Changzhou. Cai Rushan, a resident of Zhouzhuang, specialized in delivering the Zhouzhuang Minsheng Business News in the city. (2) The Finance Bureau and the Property Office will properly plan for repayment. (3) It was decided to hold a county-wide administrative meeting at 9 a.m. on the 16th of this month to discuss ways to make up the deficit.

The Detective Team Arrests a Fake Battalion Commander. Arrest for Smoking Opium Leads to Death. After Zhou returned and learned of the situation, he asked the two managers to intercede with Lu, asking him to exempt him from investigation, but Lu would only agree to drop the matter if Zhou paid 500 yuan. Zhou, unable to raise the money, secretly took a boat to Tong on the 7th to discuss the matter with his son. Lu discovered this and sent many police officers to track him down. They caught up with Zhou in Nanwanzi, Hongqiao, eight or nine li west of Juegang Street. Unexpectedly, Zhou was old and weak and was accidentally knocked unconscious by the police officers and fell into the river. He could not be rescued and died, causing a sensation in the city. Public opinion was in an uproar. The son of the deceased has heard the news and rushed back to retrieve the body and is preparing to sue the county.

Severe Thunderstorm in Yucheng. Since midnight on the 9th, there has been a severe thunderstorm in Yucheng. Although the thunder stopped on the morning of the 10th, the rain continued to pour down all day. The water level in the county river rose sharply by five feet, and the accumulated water on the ground was more than a foot deep. All major roads were blocked. The water depth in the surrounding fields was up to the chest, and agricultural crops suffered great damage. Countless thatched cottages in the fields were destroyed. On the 11th, the urban market was deserted because peddlers from the surrounding areas were blocked by the flood and could not transport goods.

Hefei 80

Nest of Bandits Raid Small Steamer. Water bandits have been discovered in Chaohu Lake in recent months, and passengers are wary. On the 7th, more than ten people, including doctor Liu Hongxun and merchant Han Shigui, were traveling by boat through Chaohu Lake and were robbed clean by bandits near Mount Mu. At noon on the 8th, a small steamer of the Three Companies sailing from Wuchao to Fei was surrounded by four or five bandit boats when it arrived at the waters of Mount Lao in Chaohu Lake. The bandits fired their guns and ordered the boat to stop. The bandits boarded the boat and searched the passengers and the staff of the disaster relief center, stealing everything and loading the stolen goods onto the boat before fleeing. Fortunately, none of the passengers were killed. The steamer arrived in Fei in the evening. According to them, several rice merchants who had come to Fei to buy rice were among the passengers and were carrying a large amount of money, so the losses were estimated at 30,000 to 40,000 yuan.

Education News Highlights

Austerity Policy for Educational Expenses in the 19th Year 81

The Ministry of Education, upon receiving an order from the Executive Yuan, informed various agencies that the proposed expenditure for the 19th year was significantly higher than the approved amount for the 18th year. After deliberation at the Political Conference, an austerity policy was adopted. The Ministry specifically notified all universities directly under its jurisdiction and the education departments and bureaus of all provinces and cities. The case was based on Executive Yuan Order No. 3205, which stated: "The attached case is based on National Government Order No. 492, which states: 'The attached case is based on a letter from the Ministry of Finance, which states that the proposed expenditure for the 19th year submitted by various agencies is higher than the approved amount for the 18th year. In view of the current financial difficulties of the country, it is necessary to consider reducing the amount. Please examine and implement accordingly.' This was resolved at the 241st meeting of this conference." [Austerity Policy] [A corresponding record of the case is hereby sent for your information and implementation]. Accordingly, the Ministry of Finance was ordered to comply and circulate the information to other agencies. In addition, the Ministry was ordered to be informed and instructed to inform all its subordinates." Except for the separate order, the Department is ordered to know this and order all subordinates to know the order.

Zhejiang University President Scheduled to Take Oath of Office 82

Proposal to Strictly Prohibit Junior High School Students from Marrying Postponed 83

The Ministry of Education received a report from the Zhejiang Education Department regarding a proposal from Li Shangchun, the principal of the private Zuoxin Junior High School in Jinhua County, requesting a general prohibition on junior high school students from marrying. Jiangsu Education Department Announces Qualified Elementary School Teachers 84

The Jiangsu Provincial Education Department issues an order informing the county education bureaus of the names of the qualified elementary school teachers of this session. The order states: "The elementary school teacher qualification examination for this session was held simultaneously in all districts except the ninth district. All examination papers have been reviewed sequentially. A total of seven candidates with a total average score of 75 or higher have been admitted as regular elementary school teachers. A total of 326 candidates with a total average score of 60 or higher have been admitted as junior elementary school teachers. In addition, one special education teacher and 621 junior elementary school specialist teachers have been admitted. In addition to publishing the names of the qualified teachers in the Provincial Government Gazette and issuing separate orders, a list of the personnel concerned is printed and sent to the bureau chief so that they can be appointed accordingly. The bureau chief should also promptly inform the teachers concerned to prepare a permit fee of one yuan and two two-inch head-and-shoulder photographs and send them to the department for review and issuance of a permit. This is of utmost importance. The order also states: "The elementary school education qualification examination for this session has been held simultaneously in all districts, and all examination papers have been reviewed sequentially. In addition to issuing separate orders to the qualified teachers, those with a total average score of less than 60 are now, in this time of scarcity of elementary school teachers, leniently admitted as junior elementary school teaching assistants for the purpose of relief. The validity period of these teaching assistants is also set at five years. During the validity period, they are only allowed to serve as junior elementary school teaching assistants. After the expiration of the period, they are not allowed to extend the period. If they wish to serve as regular junior elementary school teachers, they must pass the qualification examination again before they are allowed to serve. In addition to publishing the list of admitted personnel in the Provincial Gazette and attaching a list and issuing separate orders, the bureau chief is ordered to comply and promptly inform the teachers concerned to prepare a permit fee of one yuan and two half-length photographs and send them to the department for review and issuance of a permit. This is of utmost importance."

Jiangsu Education Department Orders the Issuance of Measures for the Transfer of State-Run Educational Institutions 85

The Jiangsu Provincial Education Department issues an order to the 61 county education bureaus, all primary and secondary schools, and all social relief institutions to issue temporary measures for the transfer of property, temporary measures for the settlement of pending cases, and a transfer form, and to comply with them. The order states: "The Provincial Government Order No. 4877 states: 'The case of the JiangSu Provincial State-run Education Agency Transfer Temporary Measures and Cleaning up Old Cases Transfer Temporary Measures submitted by the Editorial and Examination Committee was discussed at the 321st meeting of the Provincial Government Committee. The case has been reviewed and amended and is requested for consideration. The case has been approved and recorded, and the two measures are issued with this order. The department chief is ordered to conduct a thorough investigation and comply with this order.' In light of the importance of educational funding and the need for responsible custodianship, the chiefs of all educational institutions in the province have not been able to standardize the procedures for the handover of educational funding due to the lack of fixed procedures, resulting in a lack of evidence for auditing and accounting and a lack of seriousness in the handover of educational funds. In view of this, the department has drafted temporary measures for the transfer of property and temporary measures for the settlement of pending cases and submitted them to the Provincial Government Committee for review, deliberation and amendment. A notification is hereby issued. All current personnel should strictly comply with the procedures when they retire in the future. If there is any violation, they will be punished according to law. The former personnel who have not completed the transfer and acting personnel who have not settled their accounts should be ordered by the current personnel to investigate in detail and report to the department in accordance with the prescribed form within ten days of receiving this document for verification. In addition to issuing separate orders, the bureau chief is ordered to comply and instruct all subordinates to comply."

Jiangsu Provincial Temporary Measures for the Settlement of Pending Cases of Various Educational Institutions

Article 1: If the president of a state-run school, the person in charge of a social education institution, or the director of a county education bureau who left office after the reorganization in 1927 has not completed the transfer, the current person in charge should investigate the name and report it to the Education Department. If the person is currently employed in this province, their supervisor should be notified. If the person is not employed in this province, a notice should be published in the newspaper, giving them one month to return to the place where they left office and complete the settlement as soon as possible.

Article 2: The transfer should be made directly to the successor for calculation. If the direct successor is deceased or their whereabouts are unknown, the next successor in line may be assigned to take over the calculation.

Article 3: If the person who left office is unable to attend in person due to certain reasons, they may state their reasons and appoint a staff member related to the transfer case to be responsible for handling the transfer on their behalf. However, the name and position of the person handling the transfer on their behalf must be reported to the Education Department for record.

Article 4: The transfer deadline shall be handled with reference to Article 19 of the Temporary Measures for the Transfer of Educational Institutions. If several transfers are being handled at the same time, the deadline may be extended at discretion with a report.

Article 5: If the person who should be handling the transfer still fails to complete the settlement within the deadline specified in Article 1, the receiving person shall first conduct an inventory and have the supervisors or monitors calculate the amount. If there is any embezzlement or shortage, it shall be reported to the provincial government for arrest and the private property shall be seized to compensate for the loss. If the person is deceased, the estate may be executed depending on the circumstances.

Article 6: If the transfer has been completed but the settlement has not been completed, the institution shall investigate and report to the Education Department to demand a strict settlement within a deadline. If the settlement is not completed beyond the deadline, a report shall be made to the Provincial Government to stop the person from being employed by various institutions. If there is any shortage, the private property shall be seized to compensate for the loss.

Article 7: If the settlement has been completed but the payment has been delayed, the institution shall investigate and report to the Education Department to demand a strict settlement within a deadline. If the payment is not made beyond the deadline, the private property shall be seized to compensate for the loss.

Article 8: These measures shall be implemented from the date of publication of the resolution of the Jiangsu Provincial Government Committee. Attached (Investigation Form for Persons Who Have Not Completed the Transfer) Name, courtesy name, hometown, address, date of employment, date of departure, status of transfer, whether there is a shortage, current position (unfinished)

Ministry of Education Sends Personnel to Manage the Director of the Antiquities Preservation Institute 86

The Ministry of Education, in view of the fact that Wei Zhenxian, the director of the Antiquities Preservation Institute, has requested leave to return to his hometown, has specially appointed Shu Chushi, a staff member of the Social Education Department, to act as the director. In view of the news that Wei's letter to the newspaper contained the message "How can the Ministry of Education privatize antiquities?", a formal letter has been sent to correct the situation. The following is an excerpt of the explanation: (1) Wei's letter stated, "The Ministry of Education has transported away 1,084 copies of ancient books and books stored in the Nanjing Antiquities Preservation Institute." The institute's books total 1,096 copies. The Ministry believed that the institute's space was small and that it would not be able to build a reading room in a short period of time, so it ordered the books to be transported to the Ministry's library for safekeeping. When they were transported, Director Wei, for the convenience of reference, submitted a request to retain 254 copies of books related to archaeology at the institute. A total of 826 copies were actually transported to the Ministry, as documented. Sixteen copies are still missing, and the director has not submitted them for review. They are currently being investigated. The original letter stated that 1,084 copies were transported away, which is inconsistent with the facts. Moreover, the Ministry of Education is a state agency. How can the transfer of books to the Ministry for preservation be described as privatizing antiquities? (2) Wei's letter stated, "The ancient wood of the Song Dynasty was given to the private, unaccredited Datong Music Society, and Yan resigned as the director of the Nanjing Antiquities Preservation Institute as a result." In June of this year, the Datong Music Society came to the Ministry to request the wood unearthed from the Ming Palace to be used to imitate 140 kinds of ancient musical instruments with verifiable diagrams. Each type was to be made in eight copies, which were to be sent to the capital and educational and cultural institutions in various ports, as well as to Europe, the United States, and Japan. The society's aim was to restore ancient music, which was commendable. The society has been established for ten years, and all its publishing, imitation, compilation, and training work have been successful. Li Shizeng, Cai Ziming, Chu Minyi, Wang Xiaolun, and Zheng Yimen have all been executive members of the society. The Ministry of Education, which is in charge of education, promotes and rewards aesthetic education. This is one of the responsibilities of the Ministry of Education's administrative functions. The Ministry granted the request and approved the allocation, but Director Wei, who had planned to sell the wood himself (the director submitted a report to the Ministry on November 15 of last year, stating that he planned to leave a portion of the unearthed bricks and wood for preservation and sell the rest. The bricks, about 4,000 to 5,000, could be sold for four cents each, for a total of 200 yuan. The wooden boards, about 100 or so, could be sold for three yuan each, for a total of 300 yuan, and used as building materials (Director Wei submitted a report to the Ministry in June of this year, stating that if the large wooden boards unearthed from the Forbidden City were used as building materials, only the labor of workers and the cost of tiles, charcoal, and mud would be required, saving 400 yuan), was angered and resigned. (3) Wei's submission stated, "After reporting the negotiations with Zheng Yusun of the Datong Music Society, the request to excavate the ancient relics of Fenyin was rejected, and the concurrent post of editor was removed, resulting in oppression everywhere." Since Wei took office, more than one and a half years have passed. The Ministry has found that the antiquities in the institute are displayed in a disorderly manner, many of which are unnumbered. The temporary expenses that have been claimed on several occasions have not been submitted for calculation. This phenomenon may be due to the fact that the director has multiple concurrent positions and his energy is scattered, resulting in the stagnation of the institute's affairs. The institute is now in urgent need of reorganization, and the director should be required to devote himself to the affairs of the institute. Therefore, the request to excavate the ancient relics of Fenyin was rejected, and the concurrent post of editor was removed. This was purely for the purpose of reorganizing and preserving the contents of the institute. The director has combined these two matters with the case of the Datong Music Society receiving wood. (4) The current situation of the institute: Wei has now requested leave to return to his hometown. The Ministry believes that the institute is important and has sent Shu Chushi, a staff member of the Social Affairs Department, to act as the director and ordered him to reorganize the institute and number and register all the antiquities for record. When Wei left the institute, he did not register the antiquities for transfer to Shu. Therefore, the number of new and old antiquities recorded in the original letter will be reported after Shu has conducted a thorough inventory and numbering. The above items are for special correction.

Chang Shu-hong Wins Awards in France for Fine Arts 87

The Chinese students at the National School of Fine Arts in Lyon, France, have always been highly regarded by the locals for their outstanding achievements. In the school's recent academic year examinations, the Chinese student Chang Shu-hong remarkably won ten major awards. In terms of theoretical coursework, he won the first prize for artistic anatomy and the third prize for perspective. In terms of technical skills, he won the first prize and a bonus for still life drawing, the first prize and a bonus for overall average, the first prize and a bonus for the figure drawing class, the first prize and a bonus for figure sketching, the first prize for animal sketching, and the first prize across the entire school for gongbi sketching, with awards for all. Various newspapers in Lyon have reported on this event.

Introduction to Shen Yuguang's Japanese Grammar Book 90

It is truly an excellent resource for studying Japanese language in China, and everyone should have a copy. Contact: Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau, Author.

Jiangnan University Athletic Association Holds Swimming Competition 93

The Standing Committee of the Jiangnan University Athletic Association Swimming Conference held a meeting on the 10th to discuss the swimming competition rules as follows: (1) The dates of the competition are September 20th and 21st, starting at 1:00 PM each day (if there are few registrants, the competition will be completed on the first day); (2) Location: Jiaotong University swimming pool; (3) Registration deadline: September 17th; (4) Registration location: China Quan Zhuan Swimming Duty Committee, Jiaotong University; (5) Events: 50-meter freestyle, 100-meter freestyle, 400-meter freestyle, 1500-meter freestyle, 100-meter backstroke, 200-meter breaststroke, 200-meter medley relay, fancy diving (exhibition); (6) Registration forms will be dated according to the postmark date; (7) Registration forms must be signed and sealed by the physical education director and registration director of each school, otherwise they will be invalid; (8) Each school is allowed to enter four participants, and each person can participate in a maximum of three events; (9) Scoring method: The top four finishers in each event will be awarded points, with the first place receiving five points, the second place three points, the third place two points, and the fourth place one point; (10) Relay swimming will not be scored; (11) If there is a tie in total points, the order of the relay swimming will determine the championship; (12) No distinction will be made between Group A and Group B; (13) Other matters not detailed will be handled in accordance with the constitution of the Association; (14) The Duty Committee will be responsible for Jiaotong University.

Detailed Report of the Third World Women's Games, Days 2 and 3 (1) 98

(Berlin, September 8) The second and third days of the World Women's Games on the 7th and 8th of this month were met with enthusiastic audiences. Germany surprisingly surpassed Japan and took the lead in the medal count. The previous champion, the Japanese athlete, suffered a defeat and failed to maintain her dominance in the 100-meter race, only winning in the long jump. The record for long jump was 6.07 meters in the previous Games, but it regressed to 5.90 meters this time. The three events that the Japanese athlete was most confident in also regressed to second place. The overall winner in this edition of the Games was the Polish athlete Walasiewicz, who won the top spot in the 100-meter, 200-meter, and 60-meter races. The records in this edition of the Games were not particularly outstanding compared to the previous edition, except for the javelin, which produced a new world record. The results for the Czech Republic and France were not good. Japan only scored 13 points, ranking fourth. The closing ceremony was held at 6:00 PM, and the awards ceremony was held at 9:00 PM.
