Local News

Li Zhonggong, New Director-General of China Merchants Bureau, Assumes Office Yesterday 99

Wang Boqun Attended the Ceremony

Song Shuqiao Appointed Secretary-General

Li Zhonggong, the newly appointed Director-General of the China Merchants Bureau, assumed office yesterday morning at 10:00 AM in the large office hall on the second floor of the China Merchants Bureau. All the bureau's staff attended to offer congratulations. The guests included Wang Boqun, Minister of Transportation and concurrently Supervisor of the China Merchants Bureau, Liu Yunfang of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs Office, Zhuang Zhihuan, Director of the Telecommunications Department, and over ten reporters from various newspapers. The ceremony concluded at 11:30 AM. The details are as follows:

Order of Inauguration Ceremony: The inauguration ceremony had already been planned, but yesterday, an item of remarks from the Supervisor was temporarily added, as follows: (1) All stand at attention; (2) Sing the Party song; (3) Pay the highest respects to the national flag and the portrait of Dr. Sun Yat-sen; (4) Read the will of Dr. Sun Yat-sen; (5) All staff bow to the new Director-General to congratulate him on his appointment; (6) Remarks from the Supervisor; (7) Remarks from the Director-General; (8) Speeches from guests; (9) Photography.

Wang Boqun's Speech: At 9:45 AM yesterday morning, Li Zhonggong, accompanied by Cai Pei and the bureau's secretaries, arrived at the bureau. Shortly after, Wang Boqun and others also arrived in succession. The ceremony began at 10:00 AM. After the ceremony, Wang Boqun delivered a speech, stating that the China Merchants Bureau has a considerable history in China's shipping industry. Since the establishment of the national government, efforts have been made to reorganize it, but it has been subjected to pressure from imperialism and affected by the situation, coupled with the extreme lack of shipping talent in the country and the deep-seated bad habits within the China Merchants Bureau itself. As a result, the reorganization has shown little success in three years, and the government feels deeply indebted, and is very sorry to society. Comrade Zhao, who worked hard, sacrificed himself, which is even more painful. Now that the military affairs will soon end, the order in various places is gradually being restored. The national government is studying the fundamental methods for the China Merchants Bureau and has first appointed Vice Minister Li Zhonggong to take over as Director-General, acting as a Commissioner. Director-General Li has worked with me for many years and has been working hard on revolutionary work for many years and has been extremely responsible in his work. As long as the national government determines the direction, it will follow this direction, which will hopefully be more advanced than before. The fundamental issues of shipping administration are clearly stated in Dr. Sun Yat-sen's teachings and internal policies, and the government will definitely follow Dr. Sun Yat-sen's instructions to properly plan and formulate methods. Secondly, regarding the inland waterway rights, which have long been under the pressure of imperialism, the national government is also actively trying to recover them. Domestic shipping agencies should be prepared. The China Merchants Bureau is the only shipping company in our country and bears the most important responsibility. During this reorganization period, all responsible personnel should work together. I have great expectations.

Photography of Li Zhonggong's Inauguration as Director-General of the China Merchants Bureau (Photo by this newspaper)

Li Zhonggong's Speech: Subsequently, the new Director-General Li Zhonggong delivered a speech, stating that colleagues and comrades, I have been appointed to the China Merchants Bureau, and I know that my talents are insufficient to shoulder the burden, but I am obliged to do so because of the government's supervision and society's expectations, and because the China Merchants Bureau has a major mission in national economy, people's livelihood, political training, and construction, and the current problems urgently need to be solved. I do not want my personal arrival and departure to cause it to suffer unnecessary experiences in the two demands of resolving crises and striving for construction, so today I have reluctantly come to the bureau to start and do my best. At this time, I dare not say what great plans I have for the China Merchants Bureau. However, I only want to temporarily take responsibility, based on the guidance of the Central Government, to the best of my ability, in the difficulties that are generally considered difficult, and strive to overcome the difficulties with the spirit of sacrifice. Since its establishment, the China Merchants Bureau has competed with Jardine Matheson, Taikoo, and various German, Japanese, and French companies. Although it is now under pressure from the major foreign forces of Britain and Japan and is becoming increasingly difficult, it is still the only Chinese shipping company with considerable strength in the past fifty years. We cannot deny that it occupies an important position in transportation, economy, military affairs, and even national defense, culture, and foreign trade. Currently, everyone thinks that the China Merchants Bureau is in a most dangerous period, and the common lament is the overlapping debts and poor business. However, I think this is only the superficial difficulty. In addition, there are internal difficulties, namely the government, which has the responsibility of supervising and supporting the shipping industry, the shareholders who hold shares, the personnel who handle the business, and the public opinion that should bear the responsibility of guidance cannot work together and stand on the entire national and social standpoint to jointly maintain its development. The former is the result, and the latter is the cause. If the internal difficulties can be resolved, it will not only be easy to deal with the current situation, but also easy to fundamentally reorganize. Conversely, if this point is not resolved, even if some funds are raised temporarily, it will not help the fundamental plan. I very much want to find a solution to the whole problem from this factor. Dr. Sun Yat-sen analyzed in his speech on nationalism that the decline of China's shipping power was one of the reasons why foreign economic forces were able to penetrate China. This theory can be well explained by the decline of the China Merchants Bureau. I think that the shipping industry of a country, no matter which country or which ideology is established, will be difficult to resist the competition from foreign forces in this era of fierce commercial warfare and the neglect of shipping without the support of the government. However, at the same time, if a country's enterprise does not have appropriate methods to encourage national investment and protect its interests, it will be difficult for it to achieve long-term progress. I intend to determine the reorganization procedures under the principle of developing national and social enterprises and safeguarding investment interests, so that the government can choose. In other words, I want to do my best, together with my colleagues, under the guidance of the government and the supervision of the society, to directly develop business and shareholder interests, and indirectly promote national and social enterprises to a prosperous and prosperous state. As for the duties, the Second Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee decided that the reorganization of the China Merchants Bureau should be decided by a government-organized committee and appoint a commissioner to take full responsibility for the reorganization. The government has now passed the reorganization regulations. Before the committee is formed, I will act as Director-General on behalf of the Commissioner. Although I am responsible for reorganizing and managing the overall situation, the fundamental nature of the bureau, whether it is government-run, commercial-run, or jointly government-run and commercial-run, must be decided by the government. I am only one of the members who adopt the opinions of all parties and implement the government's orders, bearing the temporary responsibility of reorganization. Therefore, most of my work will have to be concentrated on resolving the current situation. Once the reorganization is slightly completed, I will resign and give way to a wise man. As for employing personnel and administration, I dare to use the four points of talent, scientific management, elimination of accumulated malpractices, and strict integrity to encourage all colleagues. I am bound by the Party and the country, and I have never acted impartially or favored anyone. I take Party discipline and national law as the standard for advancement, retreat, rewards, and penalties. I hope that all colleagues will take the interests of the Party and the country as the premise and focus on the cause of the bureau, work with peace of mind, and cooperate fully to make the difficulties that everyone sees as difficulties a new situation.

Expresses to Reporters: After Li's speech, Chen Jia of the Capital Garrison Command delivered a speech on behalf of the guests. After the photography ceremony, reporters from various newspapers visited Li to inquire about various issues of the China Merchants Bureau. Li replied that the government is still seriously considering the fundamental policy of the China Merchants Bureau. I have served in the Ministry of Communications for several years and have a general understanding of the surface of the China Merchants Bureau, but the inside is still unclear. This time, I will take some time to conduct a detailed investigation and make a systematic report for the government to decide on the policy. It is expected that the fundamental policy will be fully determined in two or three months. Maintaining the status quo is the most difficult. The bureau's scattered debts of about two million yuan urgently need to be paid. I will do my best to plan to raise two million yuan at once, so that the urgent debts can be completely cleared. Otherwise, I can only do my best to the extent of my ability, and then eliminate accumulated malpractices and save expenses, so as to gradually equalize revenue and expenditure.

Membership of the Reorganization Committee: Li also said that the number of members of the Reorganization Committee is set at nine. The reports published in the newspapers are mostly speculation and are not yet certain. The government originally intended to announce the members of the Reorganization Committee before I took office, but now it advocates postponing it, probably because it wants to fully consider the issue of personnel. The government hopes that the future Reorganization Committee will be able to do things in a practical way, otherwise it will be in vain and do nothing. The regulations for the reorganization of the China Merchants Bureau have been officially passed by the National Government Council, but they cannot be published yet. It can be revealed that the Reorganization Committee is a supervisory body. The Commissioner implements the government's decisions and takes full responsibility for the administrative implementation of the government's decisions, and cancels the current supervisory position. However, no matter how it is reformed, the rights of shareholders must be safeguarded. As for the abolition of investment interests and the forceful nationalization, this is absolutely impossible. Such unfounded rumors have repeatedly occurred in the outside world, causing misunderstandings between the government and shareholders, which also hinders the development of the bureau's affairs. It is said that Li will officially take office starting on the 15th, and will set another date to hold a supplementary swearing-in ceremony and request the National Government to send personnel to supervise the oath. Cai Pei, the former Acting Director-General, has already handed over everything and will rest in Shanghai for a while before going to Nanjing on the 15th to return to the Director of the Shipping Administration Department.

Appointment of New Staff: After the inauguration ceremony, Li met with the directors of various branch bureaus and appointed Song Shuqiao as the Secretary-General of the General Management Office, Huang Minghao as the Secretary, Lu Qinghai as the Acting Chief of the General Affairs Section, Zhou Shian as the Secretary, Kong Xiangrong as the Acting Chief of the Accounting Section, Wang Yujun as the Acting Director of the Treasury, and Zhang Yanyou as the staff member. Li then telegraphed Jiang, reporting his inauguration, briefly stating that he was serving as the Director-General of the China Merchants Bureau and concurrently Commissioner by order of the National Government. He respectfully arrived at the bureau today to take over the affairs. The swearing-in ceremony will be held at another date, and personnel will be invited to supervise the oath. The China Merchants Bureau is of great importance in military affairs, transportation, economy, and culture. Please give clear instructions at any time so that I can follow them and avoid making mistakes. I am very grateful for the opportunity to continue to report. Li Zhonggong bows respectfully.

Li's Brief Biography: Huadong News Agency reports that Li is from Guizhou, 39 years old, a member of the Chinese Nationalist Party. He graduated from the Political and Economic Department of the Beijing National College of Law and Politics in the second year of the Republic and then went to Japan to study political economy. In the fifth year of the Republic, he returned to China to participate in the anti-Yuan movement. He went to the southwest to contact the various armies of Sichuan and Guizhou to support the revolution. In the thirteenth year, he went to Guangdong to participate in the National Revolution, initially serving as the Secretary-General of the First Army of the National Revolutionary Army and the Dongjiang Pacification Committee, the Superintendent of the Chaozhou Customs, the Commissioner of Swatow, and the Chief of the Secretariat of the General Headquarters of the National Revolutionary Army. He was the Party Representative of the Twenty-first Army, a member of the Jiangxi Provisional Political Conference, and the Secretary-General of the Central Party Headquarters' Third Plenary Session. He was the Secretary-General of the Military Rehabilitation Conference of the National Revolutionary Army, the Secretary-General of the National Army Reorganization Conference, a Special Commissioner handling matters after Guizhou, a member of the Guizhou Provincial Government and concurrently Director of the Civil Affairs Department, and is currently also the Vice Minister of Transportation.

Fujian War Situation Currently in Northwest of Dehua

As for the Minister of the Navy, Yang Shuzhuang, he is currently residing in Fuzhou. When asked whether it was true that Lu Xingbang had sent troops through Shaowu and Chong'an to disturb Jiangxi and Zhejiang, Ren replied that Lu occupies Youxi and Yanping, taking advantage of the natural barriers. Now that troops are advancing to suppress him, even if Lu wanted to divide his forces to plot rebellion, he probably wouldn't have the strength. At that time, Ren was about to get into the car, so they parted ways.

Municipal Government Prepares to Establish Local Autonomy Training Institute 103

Regulations Announced Yesterday

To cultivate local autonomy talent, the municipal government will establish the Shanghai Local Autonomy Training Institute in the shortest time possible. In addition to having already assigned personnel to prepare for it, the regulations were also announced yesterday. The following is an excerpt:

Regulations of the Shanghai Local Autonomy Training Institute (Promulgated on September 12, Year 19) Chapter 1: General Provisions Article 1: This institute is established to train Shanghai local autonomy personnel. Article 2: This institute is under the Shanghai Municipal Government. Article 3: The institute shall have a director who presides over all institute affairs, concurrently appointed by the Shanghai Municipal Government from among its staff. Article 4: The institute shall have three groups: education, discipline, and administration. Article 5: The institute's teaching staff and other personnel shall be selected by the director and appointed by the mayor upon request. Article 6: The institute may employ clerks to handle copying and mimeographing matters. Chapter 2: Education Group Article 7: The education group shall have a director who, under the director's orders, presides over all educational matters. Article 8: The education group shall have two education officers who, under the director's orders and the command of the education director, shall be solely responsible for educational affairs. Article 9: The education group shall be responsible for the following duties: (1) Compiling curricula; (2) Reviewing teaching materials; (3) Assigning students to classes; (4) Registering rosters; (5) Other matters related to education. Article 10: Reforms to the institute's education and curriculum compilation may be conducted through ad hoc education meetings. Article 11: Resolutions of the education meeting shall be recorded and submitted to the director for approval. Chapter 3: Discipline Group Article 12: The discipline group shall have a director who, under the director's orders, presides over all discipline matters. Article 13: The discipline group shall have one discipline officer who, under the director's orders and the command of the discipline director, shall handle discipline matters. Article 14: The discipline group shall be responsible for the following duties: (1) Student physical education training; (2) Checking student diligence; (3) Investigating student conduct; (4) Other matters related to discipline. Chapter 4: Administration Group Article 15: The administration group shall have three administrative officers who, under the director's orders, shall be responsible for documents, accounting, and general affairs. Article 16: The administration group shall be responsible for the following duties: (1) Drafting documents; (2) Managing student accommodation; (3) Assigning duties to institute staff; (4) Ensuring cleanliness of the entire institute; (5) Managing income and expenditure; (6) Preparing budgets and final accounts; (7) Matters not belonging to other groups. Chapter 5: Students Article 17: Students shall be divided into the following two classes: (1) General Class; (2) Special Class. Article 18: The quota for general class students shall be tentatively set at 100 per term. Those who possess one of the following qualifications and pass the examination shall be admitted to the institute for training: (1) Those who have handled local administrative or autonomous affairs for more than one year and have made meritorious contributions; (2) Those who have graduated from elementary school or above, or have equivalent qualifications; (3) Those who have handled party affairs and have achieved results, as certified by the municipal party headquarters; (4) Those who have been recommended by senior officials of the current municipal government or members of the municipal committees in various districts. Article 19: The quota for special class students shall be tentatively set at 100 per term. Those who possess one of the following qualifications and pass the review shall be issued lecture vouchers by the institute to collect lectures on a termly basis: (1) Current municipal committee members and former civil servants of various agencies under the municipal government; (2) Current staff of the municipal committee offices in various districts who have made meritorious contributions. Article 20: Students of this institute shall be limited to citizens of this country. Article 21: Students must fill in a resume and application form when registering, and submit two 4-inch half-length photographs. Article 22: The main subjects of this institute are as follows: (1) The Legacy of the Premier; (2) Outline of Local Autonomy; (3) Outline of Municipal Administration; (4) Outline of Social Science; (5) Outline of Statistics. The detailed curriculum of this institute shall be compiled by the Education Group and submitted to the director, who shall forward it to the mayor for approval. Chapter 7: Training Period Article 23: The training period of this institute shall be three months, but it may be extended if deemed necessary. Article 24: Those who pass the examination after the training period shall be assigned to various district autonomy agencies for a three-month internship. Those who pass the assessment after the internship shall have the institute submit an application to the municipal government for the issuance of a training graduation certificate. Article 25: Those who fail the examination after the training or internship period may be ordered to take supplementary classes. The supplementary class period shall be limited to one month. Chapter 8: Student Benefits Article 26: Students of the general class shall have lectures and accommodation provided by the institute during the training period. Uniforms, miscellaneous expenses, and meal expenses shall be borne by the students themselves and paid to the institute for handling. Article 27: The lecture fee for the special class shall be set at five yuan, which shall be paid by the students when collecting the lecture vouchers. Chapter 9: Supplementary Provisions Article 28: If there are any matters not covered in these regulations, they may be amended at any time. Article 29: These regulations shall be implemented from the date of promulgation by the Shanghai Municipal Government.

Overseas Chinese Federation Cables for Relief to Kunming Disaster-Stricken Overseas Chinese 105

Yesterday, the Overseas Chinese Federation of the Republic of China cabled the Overseas Chinese Affairs Committee of the Central Government, the Executive Yuan of the National Government, the Ministry of Interior, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, and the Relief Committee, stating that the overseas Chinese residential area in Pontianak, the capital of the western region of Dutch Borneo, was completely destroyed by fire on the 10th of this month, with losses of approximately 4 million Dutch guilders, equivalent to over 6 million yuan in national currency. The overseas Chinese residing there are displaced. All newspapers have reported on this. It is noted that in March of the year before last, the Fujian Provincial Government provided 5,000 yuan in relief for the fire in Sibu Port, North Borneo, and the Fujian Relief Office allocated 3,000 yuan for relief. Although the amount was small, the overseas Chinese were grateful for the government's kindness and their hearts turned even more towards the motherland. This time, the number of disaster-stricken overseas Chinese in the Kunming fire is many times greater than in Sibu. The overseas Chinese in that port usually love the motherland and have spared no effort in aiding the Northern Expedition, donating to the Jinan Massacre, and various public welfare and charitable causes in the country. At this time of unexpected disaster, they must be eagerly awaiting assistance. It is earnestly requested that your committee take charge of telegraphing relief funds to be handed over to the local party headquarters and chamber of commerce for joint relief, in order to show the central government's concern for overseas Chinese in distant lands. This is respectfully reported. Respectfully, the Overseas Chinese Federation.

Japanese Attempt to Seize Chinese Silk Market in France 109

Propaganda of Japanese Cocoons Transported to China as Excuse to Suppress Chinese Silk

Commodity Inspection Bureau Sends Letter to Lyon Silk Industry to Dispel Rumors

This year's silkworm cocoon harvest in our country has decreased. Some silk merchants are deeply concerned about insufficient supply. In order to meet the urgent needs, there is talk of transporting Japanese cocoons to China. In recent years, the Japanese silk industry has developed rapidly, and it is trying to suppress the production and sales of Chinese silk. Recently, Japanese merchants have taken advantage of the rumor of Japanese cocoons being transported to China to promote in France that China's silkworm cocoon production has suddenly decreased, and that Japan is supplying the raw materials, so it would be more beneficial to directly purchase Japanese silk. If this propaganda is not dispelled immediately, it will be a major blow to Chinese silk sales in France. In view of this, the Raw Silk Inspection Office of the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau, under the direction of Director Miao, specially sent a letter to the Lyon Silk Industry Association in France, stating that the transportation of Japanese cocoons to China is only a temporary expedient, and it has not yet become a reality. Please inform the industry not to be misled by Japanese rumors in order to maintain the commercial friendship between the two countries.

Domestically Produced Hydrochloric Acid and Caustic Soda Shipped 110

Produced by Tianyuan Electrochemical Plant

Better Quality Than Foreign Goods

The Tianyuan Electrochemical Plant on Route Tenant de la Tour, sponsored by the Tianchu Monosodium Glutamate Factory, has had its machinery installed for a long time, but due to the problem of industrial salt, it has been hampered in every way. It only recently started production and shipping a few days ago. Its products, such as hydrochloric acid and caustic soda, are of sufficient grade and purity, and are highly praised by users. In addition, the bleaching powder has extremely strong bleaching power, surpassing its peers. The fresher the bleaching powder, the stronger its power. Since Japanese goods are closer to China, their power is stronger than Western goods. However, compared with the factory's local manufacturing, Japanese goods are no match. Currently, orders are pouring into the factory from as far south as Guangdong and as far north as Liaoning, and there is a shortage of supply. However, it is heard that the second batch of raw materials cannot be transported to Shanghai because the weighing and measuring bureau at the place of origin did not weigh and release them. It is feared that production will have to be stopped again. It is hoped that the government will support industry and release the goods for transportation as soon as possible.

Business Community Today Mourns Chen Qinxuan 112

In the Third Year of the Republic's Punitive Expedition Against Yuan

Saved Millions of Lives

Chen Qinxuan, a major figure in Shanghai's shipping industry and owner of the Yuanyi Steamship Company, whose courtesy name was Zhongshu, was from Zhenhai County, Zhejiang Province. He initially worked for the British-American Tobacco Company and was promoted to an important position. Later, he established his own Yuanyi Steamship Company with five ships sailing in the North and South Seas, and he pioneered the joint Shanghai-Liaoning-South Manchuria transportation of Chinese ships, which is still convenient for merchants and travelers today. However, during the decline of the shipping industry, Chen supported it for six or seven years. Due to poor business, the ships were all mortgaged and eventually closed down. Chen's efforts were also exhausted. He repeatedly tried to recover, but was always thwarted by the environment and unable to revive. Last autumn, he retired to recuperate and initially contracted hemoptysis. The illness deepened this spring and he died on August 6, at the age of 42, leaving behind six children, the eldest son being 15 and still in school, and the eldest daughter about to marry this winter. The family is impoverished. Shanghai business figures Yu Qiaqing, Wen Lanting, Yuan Ludeng, Wang Xiaolai, etc., believe that Chen not only contributed to the recovery of shipping rights but also made great contributions to the revolutionary cause. In the third year of the Republic, Chen Ying士 planned the punitive expedition against Yuan in Shanghai, ordering Niu Yongjian and Liu Fubiao to attack the Manufacturing Bureau on June 19 and fight with Zheng Rucheng. At that time, the party army failed due to lack of supplies. Zheng Rucheng sent an ultimatum from a German engineer in the factory to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, limiting the party army to withdraw within 24 hours, otherwise, artillery would be fired. At that time, the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce was presided over by Mo Zijing, Li Pingshu, Zhu Shaosu, etc. After receiving the letter, they were greatly frightened because the lives and property of more than one million residents in southern Shanghai were at stake. They urgently replied to Zheng to stop the firing, but at that time, communication had been cut off and someone had to be sent to deliver the letter, but no one dared to enter the tiger's den. Chen was then serving as a staff officer and consultant to the Chamber of Commerce's punitive expedition against Yuan. Considering the safety of hundreds of thousands of people in the city, he resolutely stepped forward and borrowed a small boat from the British Navy to venture into the line of fire. After various dangers, he was detained by Zheng's troops several times and finally arrived at Zheng's headquarters. When Chen left, it was originally agreed that the time limit was one o'clock in the middle of the night. If he did not return by one o'clock, he would be killed. He did not return until two o'clock. Everyone thought he must have been killed by Zheng, but he succeeded in returning. Zheng Rucheng did not fire the artillery. Chen's sacrifice to enter the dangerous place to protect the safety of hundreds of thousands of residents in southern Shanghai was a great contribution. Niu Yongjian and others were personally involved in this matter. Now, Yu Wang Zhu and others have scheduled to mourn Chen today at the Customs Office in Nanshi and plan to state the facts of his merits and ask the National Government for a pension.

Shanghai Port's Exports to the United States in August 113

According to the American Evening News, according to statistics from the US Consulate General, the value of exports from Shanghai to the United States in August was 1,798,469 gold yuan, bringing the total value for the previous seven months to 28,715,961 gold yuan. The value of goods shipped to the United States that month was relatively low, accounting for only one-sixteenth of the total value for the eight months. Textiles and raw materials still accounted for the largest value of goods, totaling 1,328,500 gold yuan, which still accounts for slightly more than one-sixteenth of the total value of 20,303,708 yuan for the eight months. In addition, the value of goods shipped from Shanghai to the Philippines in August was 252,591 gold yuan, and the total value for the eight months was 1,837,107 gold yuan, with fresh eggs being the largest commodity. The export value in August was 102,206 gold yuan, accounting for 40% of total exports. In addition, exports to Honolulu were valued at 5,737 gold yuan, and the total value for the eight months was 53,482 gold yuan, with ceramics being the largest commodity. The August value of 1,323 yuan also accounted for 23% of total exports.

Qingyunli Demolition Dispute 114

Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce Requests the Municipal Council to Issue Licenses Carefully

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the Municipal Council yesterday regarding the Qingyunli demolition dispute, stating: "We hereby inform you that the houses in the Qingyunli area on North Sichuan Road, Chongming Road, are being demolished by the owner, Sassoon & Co., under the pretext of renovation, using more than 200 White Russian workers, causing disturbances that resulted in injuries to three tenants. The merchants among the tenants have also suffered damage to their goods during the brick and tile chaos. Our association has recently received a report from the Guang Miscellaneous Goods Trade Association, whose members have suffered losses due to this case. They have attached photos and requested us to send a letter to the Municipal Council to handle it impartially. We have investigated that Sassoon & Co. wants the tenants to move out and take back the houses for renovation. It should file a lawsuit in court to recover the houses in accordance with legal procedures, and it must not use such direct action to obstruct public order. Although the landlord's recovery of the houses is an exercise of its due rights, the exercise of rights has certain procedures and certain limits. If it does not resort to the law but directly resorts to force, it will not only cause unexpected losses to the other party but will also affect innocent third parties, which can lead to major disturbances at any time. This is not allowed in a country with a little legal order. It is true that there are many landlords in the Public Concession who want to recover their houses and proceed in accordance with the proper procedures, but it is also common to take direct action to demolish houses to force tenants to move out. This kind of despotic means of landlords is almost non-existent in the entire country except in the Public Concession. If there is such a thing, it is difficult to escape the punishment of the law. Now that such a major disturbance of destroying property and injuring people has occurred, our association believes that the Municipal Council should formulate appropriate regulations to prevent such direct actions in the future. When issuing demolition licenses, it must be verified that there are no disputes or that the eviction has been approved in accordance with legal procedures before issuing the license. Otherwise, the landlords will use the demolition license as a weapon to force tenants out. This should be paid attention to by the Municipal Council. Secondly, it is also a question of whether the landlord has applied for a demolition license. According to reports, the site has not been fenced off, which seems to prove that the license has not been obtained. If this is true, the Municipal Council should prosecute the landlord for violating the regulations of the Concession. Thirdly, the three tenants who were injured this time were found to have been injured by demolition workers. The Municipal Council should also instruct the police to file separate lawsuits with the court for punishment. As for the main point, it is necessary to formulate appropriate regulations for demolition licenses in the future and carefully examine and approve them so that landlords will not use their power to the fullest extent, which can reduce the medium of social disturbances. A letter is prepared for this purpose and returned, and you are requested to investigate and handle it accordingly. This is addressed to the Public Concession Municipal Council."

Baoshan County Held County Administration Meeting Yesterday 117

Red Cross Modifying Constitution Committee Continues Meeting 119

The Chinese Red Cross Modifying Constitution Committee held its ninth meeting on September 12 at 2:00 PM. The following members were present: Li Zhenbang, Wen Lanting, Jiang Daqiu, Yang Ke, Xu Xichun, Wang Peiyuan, Wu Jiasan, Ye Zhisheng, Dong Xinqin, Xue Shaoting, Hong Yanbin, Wang Xiaolai. Chairman Wen Lanting presided and Secretary Wei Ruifeng recorded. (1) The chairman reported on the by-laws of the second sub-committee. Jiang Daqiu proposed that the first article should be changed to: "The sub-committee is organized in accordance with the articles of the Chinese Red Cross and these by-laws." (2) Yang Ke proposed that the phrase "all the rights that can be enjoyed in the sub-committee" in the ninth article should be changed to "all members of the sub-committee should fulfill the same obligations and enjoy the same rights. When a member of the sub-committee transfers, they should submit the documents to their sub-committee for verification by the General Association, and pay a participation fee of one yuan." Xu Xiongchun seconded. (3) Jiang Daqiu proposed that articles 11, 12, and 13 should be renumbered as Chapter 3, and the phrase "committee affairs" in Chapter 3 is inappropriate and should be changed to "organization and reading." According to the Red Cross articles, the example that should be changed and should be drafted by Jiang Xuanqiu, from article 11 to article 26, a total of 16 articles, was read article by article. A majority approved. (4) Xu Xichun proposed that item 5 of article 26 should be changed to: "All the above-mentioned assets should be submitted to the General Association and then to the National Government for filing." (5) Jiang Daqiu proposed that article 27 should be changed to: "Two or three property managers of the sub-committee shall be elected by the board of directors." (6) The chairman proposed that the first item of the appendix should be changed according to the Red Cross articles to: "These by-laws will take effect after being passed by the general assembly of members and submitted to the National Government for approval and filing." (7) The chairman proposed that the second reading of the sub-committee's by-laws has been completed today. The third reading will continue tomorrow. If there is time, the election law for standing members will be read for the third time. The meeting adjourned at 5:00 PM after the by-laws of the sub-committee were discussed.

Local News (Continued)

Female Opera Singer Mao Jianpei Dies Young 120

Lover's Suspicion Was Unavoidable

Taking Poison to Prove Her Innocence Was Truly Lamentable

Alas, a Song of Love

Henceforth, the Face and Peach Blossoms

The pearl in the palm of famous actor Mao Yunke, Mao Jianpei, at the young age of twenty-three, was renowned for both her talent and beauty. She once appeared on the silver screen, earning the title of "Star," and her beauty became even more famous. She was deeply accomplished in Peking Opera, specializing in Qingyi and Huashan roles, and could perform many plays with great acclaim, no less than her father. Various Shanghai stages competed to hire her with high salaries, demonstrating her artistic talent. Ms. Mao was still unmarried, due to her father's exceptionally strict criteria for choosing a son-in-law. Last summer, she performed in Hankou, and this spring, she returned to Shanghai with honors, residing with her younger brother, Yanqiu (age twenty, specializing in Huashan roles), in a self-built mansion at No. 214, the corner of Xiafei Road and Songshan Road in the French Concession. They only employed a few servants for their needs, while their father, Yunke, resided separately in a villa on Guling Road. Suddenly, according to a friend's urgent report, Ms. Mao recently, due to a marriage issue, secretly ingested opium, resulting in her tragic death. Here is a record of public sentiment:

He Hou Scolds the Palace

Voice and Appearance Both Excellent

Mao Jianpei was born on the seventh day of the ninth lunar month, with the nickname Jiu'er, hence people referred to her as Miss Jiu. She was intelligent, lively, and exceptionally gifted. She initially joined China Film Company, playing a key role in the play "Face and Peach Blossoms."

Appearing on the silver screen was just right, but her father, Yunke, strongly disapproved of his beloved daughter's involvement in film and was very determined to prevent it. He urged her to study Peking Opera. Jianpei was exceptionally clever and soon mastered the essence of Qingyi. Her father, Yunke, wanting his daughter to further her studies, sent Jianpei north the year before last to become a disciple of Wang Yaoqing. Under the guidance of a famous teacher, her skills improved rapidly. Upon returning to Shanghai, she accepted an engagement from the Danggui First Stage and began her stage life. Her first performance was "He Hou Scolds the Palace," and her excellent voice and appearance were greatly appreciated by the audience. After the Danggui ceased performances, she went to Hankou.

Shanghai Residents Look Forward To

New Autumn Performance

This past March, Jianpei returned from Hankou and resided at No. 214 Xiafei Road, living a secluded life, using acting as a pastime. In the summer, the owner of the Sanxing Stage persuaded Mao Yunke to have his beloved daughter perform at the beginning of autumn to satisfy Shanghai's admiration for Miss Jiu's voice and appearance. Mao agreed and made a contract, choosing the 28th of this month to take the stage. The week before last, her father invited friends and companions to visit Jianpei and introduce her to the public. Every night, he also supervised his daughter's vocal practice at his residence on Guling Road to prepare.

Hankou Lovers

Agreed to Marry

Mao Jianpei's sudden death is indeed abrupt. Just three days ago, someone encountered her at her residence on Guling Road. According to the reporter's investigation from various sources, her death is indeed confirmed. However, the cause of death has slight discrepancies in the rumors. Here is a description of what has been heard and is reliable: Mao Jianpei's death was a suicide, and the main reason involved a marriage issue. It is said that a Mr. Hu met Jianpei during a trip to Hankou and fell in love, agreeing to marry each other. However, Jianpei was very filial to her father and did not want to make decisions about marriage on her own. She once said to Mr. Hu, "I am currently twenty-three years old. The matter of marriage should wait two more years before it can be held because my father has spent a lot of money and energy on my acting training. I should try to repay him a little to comfort my father." Her intention was that in these two years, she would use her performance income to support her father.

Buying a Car for Transportation

Caused a Major Uproar

Mr. Hu also came to Shanghai with Jianpei on this trip, and the two were very close. Recently, Mr. Hu wanted to buy a car for transportation and entrusted Jianpei to choose and buy it. Mao had a female friend, Mrs. Min, whose husband knew car dealers, so she transferred the request to contact the car dealership. However, Hu thought Mao's car purchase was not straightforward and went directly to the car dealership, entrusting Mr. Min instead. He felt very unhappy in his heart and suspected that Min was also young and seemed quite familiar with Mao, creating clouds of suspicion. His words often revealed displeasure. Mao knew his intention and went to Min's place to cancel the car purchase the next day. Who knew that Mr. Hu would go to Mao's residence at this time and, finding her absent, inquired and learned that she had gone to Min's place, leading to a misunderstanding and a major uproar.

Taking Poison to Prove Her Innocence

Tragic Death

That night, the two met and had a big argument. Mao Jianpei had always been ambitious and proud. In a moment of anger, she conceived the idea of suicide and secretly swallowed a large amount of opium. Her father noticed that she was already poisoned and immediately hired a car to send her to the hospital for treatment, but it was impossible to save her, resulting in her tragic death. The above is from reliable sources. However, although the reporter has no doubt that Mao Jianpei committed suicide, whether there are other details is unknown to outsiders. For the sake of caution, the reporter visited her father, Mao Yunke, at his residence on Guling Road.

Heartache and Tears

Old Father's Sorrow

The reporter arrived at Mao's residence on Guling Road and presented his card. Jianpei's father, Yunke, came out to see him, with worry visible between his eyebrows and tears welling up in the corners of his eyes, as if telling people about the grief and pain of his beloved daughter's death. The reporter asked about Jianpei's death, and Mao nodded repeatedly, sighing incessantly, saying, "My little girl was originally going to make her debut, who knew such a thing would happen, alas!" The reporter asked, "What disease did your beloved suffer from that caused her death?" Mao paused slightly, his face showing sadness, and said, "She suffered from a very serious liver and stomach problem and died from it." The reporter further inquired about the exact time of Jianpei's death. Mao Yunke claimed that his mind was confused and he could not remember. He turned to his third daughter and said, "When did your sister die, do you know?" His daughter said tearfully, "It was at seven o'clock last night."

A Song of Love

Then Departed from the World

At this point in the conversation, Mao Jianpei's art friend, Brother Guo, entered the room and, seeing the reporter, sighed with regret and spoke of the dying state of Miss Jiu, which was heartbreaking. After Mao Jianpei took poison, she was sent to Shanghai Nursing Home on Luo Biegen Road. By the evening of the 12th, around 7 p.m., her condition suddenly changed. However, a final glow appeared, and a faint blush appeared on her jade-like face. At this time, dusk had arrived, and the setting sun had just receded. The lights had just come on, and a pale yellow halo appeared in the sky. The sickroom became even quieter. Suddenly, a sharp singing voice was heard from Mao Jianpei's bedside, mournful and beautiful, unbearable to hear. Many Westerners in the nursing home were recuperating, and they leaned their ears to listen and couldn't help but get up and inquire, knowing that it was the mournful song of a Chinese girl on her deathbed. They all shed tears of sadness. It turned out that Jianpei's song was a song from the "Extravagant History of the Xuan Palace." The song was "Dream Lover." Almost as soon as she finished singing, the protagonist of "Face and Peach Blossoms" passed away forever. Hearing this song, the reporter couldn't help but feel sad, while the deceased's father, Yunke, stared straight at the reporter in the light with a pale and sorrowful face, silently. Mao Jianpei's remains were moved to the Universal Funeral Home yesterday for the main burial. However, the location of the resting place has not yet been decided.

Robbery of Huge Sum of Money in the Early Morning 121

Two Bags of Banknotes, Over Eight Thousand Dollars

Robbers Fired Shots as a Warning After the Robbery

At Bao Da Xiang Foreign Goods General Store, located at No. 90 to No. 100, the corner of Tongyun Street and Xiaodongmen Main Street in the French Concession, yesterday morning at around 8 a.m., the old clerks Lin Chusheng (26 years old) and Zhang Axiang (40 years old, both from Ningbo) were ordered to deliver banknotes worth 8,312 yuan and a paper of 40 liang of silver drafts. The cash was divided into two bags, with Lin and Zhang each carrying one bag, intending to deliver them to the Hongcheng Money Exchange on Ningbo Road. Unexpectedly, while passing the Zuibaoyuan Hotel on Tongyun Street, four robbers suddenly appeared. Two robbers held guns against Lin and Zhang's chests, threatening them to keep silent. They took all the banknotes in the two bags. At that time, a Bao Da Xiang apprentice, Gu Zhongfang, was out buying glutinous rice cakes and caught a glimpse of the scene. He immediately blew the whistle, and the robbers turned around and fired two shots as a warning. At that time, Shi Ziyun (28 years old), a local worker from the Jinxin Laundry Shop, which was next to Zuibaoyuan, went out to get an iron. A bullet flew and grazed his right leg, fortunately without serious injury. The robbers carried the stolen goods, escaped through the back door of the Yuebin Hotel, exited from the front door, and fled to the Chinese Concession, where they disappeared. The two old clerks, Lin and Zhang, returned to the store and reported to the Xiaodongmen Police Station, requesting an investigation. They also stopped payment of the drafts at the money exchange.

The Police Station Has Sent a Telegram to Inquire

Await a Reply Before Sending Personnel to Bring Him Back

In the case of the robbery of 100,000 yuan in banknotes from the Zhejiang Provincial Bank, the Laozha Police Station Detective You A Gen has arrested several robbers in the Chinese and foreign concessions. The military police in Tianjin have also intercepted Zhu Dexin, the main culprit who fired shots during the robbery. Personnel have already been dispatched to Tianjin to bring him back. After the police station obtained the names of the four main robbers from the arrested thief He Guo, they immediately telegraphed major ports and commercial cities, ordering strict investigation of incoming ships and trains. Now that Zhu Dexin has been arrested in Tianjin, the other three robbers are expected to have fled far away. Yesterday, it was reported that the Hong Kong authorities also arrested a robber in this case when a ship from Shanghai arrived in Hong Kong. The police station has now sent a telegram to inquire. Once the Hong Kong side replies and confirms the report, detectives will be selected and sent to Hong Kong to bring him back.

Huang Bohui Case: Kidnappers Sentenced to Death 123

Female Kidnapper's Sentence Reduced to 20 Years

Mr. Huang Bohui, general manager of the Shi Bao newspaper, was kidnapped in front of the newspaper office along with his car and held for ransom in a small boat on the Hexi countryside's Jiangbei River. The city's Public Security Bureau's water and land police rescued Mr. Huang on the night of the kidnapping and arrested Zhou Wu and Li Wangshi, who were guarding the hostage. A handgun with six live rounds was found on them. They were transferred to the Special District Local Court for trial. Yesterday morning was the day for the verdict in this case. Mr. Huang arrived at the court's First Criminal Court at 9 a.m. to await the announcement. Subsequently, Criminal Court President Xu Jia Shi ascended the seat, ordered the male and female criminals to be brought forward, briefly questioned their names, and then read the main text of the verdict: Zhou Wu was sentenced to death for the crime of jointly kidnapping for ransom. Li Wangshi's sentence for the crime of jointly kidnapping for ransom was reduced to 20 years of imprisonment. The handgun and bullets were confiscated. After the verdict, the police took the two criminals away for separate detention, awaiting execution after confirmation.

Notorious Zhejiang Province Robbers Arrested in Shanghai 124

False Letter of Appointment Seized

All Sentenced to the Headquarters

Yongkang County, Zhejiang Province, has been repeatedly ravaged by bandits this year. Residents have been killed and occupied villages and towns have been almost completely devastated. They reported to the Laozha Police Station the day before yesterday, who, together with detectives Wang Shusheng, Zhao Gengsheng, and Western detectives, went to the hotel. All five bandits were in the room and were arrested together and taken back to the police station for questioning. It was learned that bandit Lü also had another residence at No. 2 Sanrui Lane, Lafayette Road in the French Concession. They cooperated with French police detectives and went to the address, where they found a letter of appointment from Zhou Fengqi, the former commander of the 26th Army. The false position appointed was "Deputy Captain of the Fourth Detachment of the First Brigade of the Second Route Mobile Army of the Republic of China Army," while the same person also signed in the name of the Brigade Commander. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the Special District Local Court, where Presiding Judge Xu Jiashi reviewed the case and clearly ordered that Lü Sitang and the other four be taken by the detectives of the Headquarters to be investigated.

Zhang Taijie's Appeal Case 125

Tried Yesterday at the Jiangsu High Court

Dong Yu and Four Others Did Not Attend

The case of Zhang Taijie, general manager of the Sichuan-Hankou Railway, being accused by Zeng Xianzhi of embezzling more than 3 million taels of huge sums of money, appealed to the High Court after being dissatisfied with the verdict of the Shanghai Local Court. On the 21st of last month, Criminal Division Chief Lin Dawen opened an investigation court to summon Zhang Taijie and Zeng Xianzhi, Dong Yu, Ao Enzhan, and others to inquire about the details, as reported in this newspaper. Yesterday (13th), High Court Chief Lin continued to open the court. Those summoned included Dong Yu, Li Shirui, Cheng Zhongfan, Ao Enzhan, Wu Jingming, and five others. All failed to report due to other matters, so only Zhang Taijie was summoned for questioning. Details are recorded as follows:

Case History: On June 25th of the lunar calendar in 1929, Zhang Taijie, Chen Shujia, Liu Yajue, Wu Jingming, and others established the Sichuan-Hankou Railway Resident Office in Shanghai. They mortgaged the Hankou Shanghai land to Ao Enzhan for 5,000 yuan, with Ao first paying 2,500 yuan to cover the opening expenses. However, after obtaining the funds, Zhang used all of them. Subsequently, he sent someone to Cheng Xuelou to request the return of the previous loan road deed. Cheng's son, Zhongfan, handed it over, and Zhang immediately mortgaged it to lawyer Li Shirui for 20,000 yuan. He used this money to repay Ao Enzhan's loan (2,500 yuan) and to reward those who contributed and pay the lawyer Dong Yu's signature fee. The remaining funds were embezzled by Zhang Taijie. Later, Zeng Xianzhi came forward to report it. The Shanghai Local Court sentenced Zhang to three years of imprisonment, while lawyer Dong Yu was declared innocent.

Court Hearing: Yesterday afternoon at around 2 p.m., Chief Lin Dawen brought Zhang Taijie to court and informed him that today's investigation court was still open because Dong Yu and Li Shirui had not attended. Although Dong Yu had been found not guilty, the outcome of the appeal trial was also unknown. In other words, Dong was still an appellant in this case and not a witness. Xiaodongmen Minguo Road 127

Silk and Satin Industry Nakedly Competing with Low Profits

Gathering New Autumn Seasonal Weavings

Displaying the Storefront for People to Visit

Sacrificing Capital to Set Low Prices

The Principle is to Sell More and Not Seek High Profits

Hongzhang Silk and Satin Bureau on Minguo Road, Xiaodongmen, South Shanghai, opened in September of yesteryear and has become famous far and wide in less than a year. As for the latest invention, Hongzhang silk, the texture is solid and soft, excellent in color and long-lasting. There is also an unprecedented great sacrifice in the silk industry, which is to cut open the original piece, classify it for retail, give enough size, and reduce the price, so that customers can easily purchase and get unexpected bargains, come out of interest and return happily. Therefore, the ability to promote has been universally praised and there is no need to repeat it. Continuing to invent Prosperous Ling, Economic Ge, and various noble products, the colors are excellent, and everyone is happy to buy them. The bureau is flattered and is now preparing goods to strive for perfection and always adhere to the principle of low profits. At this time, the new autumn season is approaching, and people from all walks of life are eager to add new clothes. The bureau, in view of this, selects and handles the latest and most fashionable silk fabrics for men and women, such as satin brocade, patterned and plain wool Ge, exotic printed soft satin brocade, patterned Xiang Ling, new patterned Ling, power lubrication, brocade crepe, and various colors are full of shelves. On September 13th, a big autumn sale will be held, with price cuts implemented. Each item will be marked with low ["Special Price Red Code"] to show sincerity. As for Hongzhang silk, due to the soaring raw material prices and increased costs, the bureau is striving to promote it and will still not increase the price. During the discount period, Hongzhang silk will still be sold at half price on the market, such as men's robe fabric sold for only 5.5 yuan, such as cheongsam fabric sold for only 3.5 yuan, men's and women's pants fabric sold for only 1.9 yuan, cheongsam pants fabric sold for only 1.5 yuan, men's and women's vest fabric sold for only 1.1 yuan. The second-floor foreign goods department has complete colors and adds two inches to the scale. The second-floor bargain department has a special cheap separate clothing department. There are thousands of pieces of new clothing fabrics, and the colorful colors are piled up like mountains. There is a special mail order department for speedy mail order with the original return of parts and self-supplied postage. The gift voucher department has exquisite printing of thirteen-color gift vouchers that are rich and trustworthy. The congratulatory axis department delivers documents quickly and the prices are low.

Expert in Writing Threatening Letters 128

Fang Pingyi Fully Confesses

Nearly Twenty Times in Total

Yu Maolong, a detective from the First District Police Station in the South City, recently discovered that Fang Zhen, alias Pingyi, a Ningbo native who habitually wrote threatening letters to extort money in the South City area, was hiding in the pavilion room at No. 3 Zaihua Lane, Xiaoximen. The night before last, he led a group of detectives to the Second Branch of the Second District Police Station, requesting the dispatch of police officers and detective Yuan Haishan and others, a total of more than ten people, to quietly surround the front and rear doors of Zaihua Lane. Detectives Yu and Yuan entered and arrested Fang Pingyi, the extortionist, and delivered him to the police station yesterday for interrogation. According to the confession of the extortionist, he is 17 years old, from Zhenhai. He came to Shanghai in the first month of the lunar calendar last year. He currently has no business. He used to live at the Xiaojiu Hua Fukang Candy Store and worked at the racetrack before moving to the pavilion room at No. 3 Zaihua Lane, Xiaoximen, in February this year, where he slept on the floor. The monthly rent of four yuan was paid by pawning clothes. Now, due to a lack of resources, he wrote threatening letters. The first time was in April, writing to Chen Longlian in Bai Zha Lane three or four times without success. He also sent someone to speak to him. The second time was in May, writing to Jiang Baokang in Huangjia Que, Xiaoximen, three times without success. He heard that someone was coming to arrest him. The third time was to Zhang Yingcai at No. 122 Nancang Street in June, but only wrote one letter. Someone came to arrest him, but it was also unsuccessful. The fourth time was to the Zhang family (no name given) at No. 123 Shangwen Road in June, writing three letters, but someone came to arrest him, so he stopped. The fifth time was in June at 10 PM, writing to Lu Chuping in Fu'an Lane, Dongjiadu, writing twice, but someone came to arrest him, so he stopped. The sixth time was in June at 10 PM, writing to the Wang family on Zhonghua Road, Laoximen, writing three times, but they ignored him. The seventh time was in June, writing to the Zhu family on Zhonghua Road, Dananmen, writing four or five times, but they also ignored him. The eighth time was writing to Dr. Tan Ganchen, writing two letters, but it was also ineffective. The ninth time was writing to the Peng family at the New Wharf, writing twice, but as a result, they sent someone to arrest him. His relatives run the Huiwen Tang Bookstore on Qipan Street and is his maternal uncle. Also, Xu Fu at No. 25 Deqing Lane, Tongfu Lane, Julaida Road in the French Concession is his maternal uncle. They can be inquired. He did not move any silver dollars, but at the beginning of last month, he wrote a letter to Chen Budan at No. 102 Anlan Road and received 20 silver dollars. He went to collect it at 6 PM, and only saw a child, not an adult, etc. It is reported that the case is currently summoning the victims to the police station to testify before being sent to the General Bureau for transfer to the court for trial.

Public Notice by the Municipal Public Security Bureau Regarding Rent Arrears 132

Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau Public Notice Zheng Zi No. 25: This city is an important commercial port in the country, with Chinese and foreigners living together, and attracting attention from both domestic and foreign quarters. In order to promote the development of the entire city, it is necessary to attract merchants and residents so as to gather people from all directions and achieve prosperity day by day. The first step is to build more city houses and residences so as to fully accommodate them as the only fundamental plan. Recently, it has been found that the construction in the concession is becoming newer and more prosperous every day, with almost no vacant land, while the city is sparsely populated and progress has been slow in recent years. Tracing the cause, it is the concession tenants who are accustomed to being lazy and rely on arrears of rent as a common occurrence, often delaying payment for months or years. As the arrears accumulate, they become increasingly unable to pay, and in the end, they can only resort to the law or reluctantly settle by vacating and returning the house. Landlords have no interest to account for on time, and there are complicated lawsuits, so adding one business increases one burden. Therefore, powerful families are unwilling to invest in construction, and the completed houses are not repaired in time and gradually become dilapidated. If this continues, not only will future construction be impossible, but the existing city will also gradually decline. If active measures are not taken to remedy this situation, the future of the city will be greatly hindered. It is found that rights and obligations should be equal. Landlords buy land and build houses and manage laboriously. Tenants enjoy the right to reside in an existing house and should bear the obligation to pay rent on time. People who rent houses also have their own occupations, either shop owners or laborers. If goods are taken without payment or labor is not compensated, how can this be justified? Landlords are also operating a business, so how can they invest in property without any reasonable return? This bureau is responsible for maintaining public safety, and all threats to public order must be prevented in advance. Regarding the matter of rent arrears, the Municipal Government has recently issued an order to ban it, and it should be handled in earnest according to the powers. In addition to issuing an order to subordinates to comply, this notice is issued for public knowledge. If any arbitrary rent arrears are found in the future, the owner will immediately report the case and strictly ban it without any leniency. All residents of this territory must comply. This notice is issued on the thirteenth day of the ninth month of the nineteenth year of the Republic of China. Director Yuan Liang.

Three Cases Arising from Opium 136

Divorce... Insulting Elders... Smoking

Tang Zuyao, a villager from the Third Map of the 29th Bao of Hongqiao Road, West Shanghai, is addicted to opium. His wife, Gu, advised him to quit, but he became irreconcilable with his wife. He filed a divorce suit against his wife in the local court, but it was rejected. Not long after Tang read the verdict, he requested another divorce, so the case is still pending. Gu, being a traditional woman, did not want a divorce and cried to Tang's paternal uncle, Tang Heting, asking him to help reconcile. Tang Heting repeatedly tried to persuade Zuyao, but Zuyao refused. Heting could not help but scold him, but he was beaten by Zuyao. After Heting was injured, he went to the local court to report that Zuyao should not beat and insult his elders. After the prosecutor verified the injury, he issued an arrest warrant the day before yesterday, and the bailiff went to arrest him. Zuyao was still indulging in opium, so his smoking paraphernalia was also seized by the bailiff. Together with Tang Zuyao's arrest, the preliminary trial order was issued to detain him pending punishment, so the matter that started with opium ended with opium, suddenly turning into three cases.

Negotiations Over Workers Beating Police 137

Trouble Started from Gambling

At the Sixth District, Second Branch of the Shanghai West Xujiahui Town Municipal Public Security Bureau, at around 8 PM the night before last (12th), Patrol Officer Xu Guifang of the Jinji Bridge Police Station reported that Zhu Zizhen and Zeng Yunzhong, workers from the Yougeng Taihe Joint Flour Factory, and Wu Guisheng, a worker from the Dachina Rubber Factory, had a quarrel in Taiyuan Lane in the French Concession due to gambling, resulting in a fight. Zeng and Zhu were no match and fled into the Chinese territory, but Wu Guisheng refused to give up and gathered six or seventy workers from the same factory, creating a menacing scene. They then chased after them to the south end of Jinji Bridge (which belongs to Chinese territory). Patrol Chief Wang Dazhao and Police Officer Xie Yongzhang saw this and, fearing trouble, stepped forward to stop them. However, the workers ignored the warnings and dragged Patrol Chief Wang and Police Officer Xie into the French Concession north of the creek, surrounded and beat them. He requested the dispatch of police to rescue them. After receiving the report, Director Liu, together with Patrol Officer Yuan Gancheng and Patrol Chief Shi Hegen, led the police to suppress the situation. Upon arrival, they found that the French Concession police had dispatched detectives and arrested seven rubber factory workers, including Wu Guisheng, while the rest fled. Wang and Xie were also taken back to the police station and sent to Renji Hospital for treatment. They were discharged after bandaging because their injuries were not serious. Director Liu returned to the station and prepared a letter to the police station, personally going to welcome and retrieve the head of the arrest. Because the case had been reported to the General Patrol Room Detective Division, he had to wait until 9 AM tomorrow (i.e., the 13th) to welcome and retrieve them from the Lujiazui Police Station. Director Liu repeatedly negotiated with him but did not get any results. He had to bring Wang and Xie back to the police station. Yesterday morning, Director Liu went to the Lujiazui Police Station with Patrol Officer Yuan to welcome and retrieve the murderers Wu Guisheng and others. After Director Liu repeatedly negotiated with the police station, five people were handed over only at around 1 PM (one of them was released by the detective, and Jiang Zhongying's leg was injured and treated in the hospital). Director Liu brought them back to the station and conducted a strict interrogation. According to Wu Guisheng, 30 years old, Yu Changfu, 27 years old, Zhang Jinyang, 25 years old, Shen Baosheng, 19 years old, and Zhang Xinfu, 16 years old, all workers in the factory, they went out to see what was happening and were mistakenly arrested. They firmly denied beating the patrol chief. Wang Patrol Chief and Xie Police Officer were summoned for questioning. They claimed that a total of seven people were arrested at the time, brought back to Fuxing Road by detective Hong Debao of the Shanzhong Road Police Station, and one person was released by Detective Hong. They also pointed out that the arrested criminals were indeed the perpetrators at the scene and presented the torn uniforms, military caps, and weapons for inspection. After Director Liu's confession, he immediately dispatched police to arrest Zhu Zizhen and Zeng Yunzhong, workers from the Gengtai Factory, who were the real instigators of the case. The workers dared to gather and beat the patrol chief, which was a blatant disregard for the law. He prepared a document to send all the criminals to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for strict legal action. Detective Hong Debao privately released criminals halfway through, and a serious negotiation should be made with the police station.

Industrial Unions Must Not Suspend Activities of Various Labor Unions 139

Circular from the Citizens Training Committee

The Shanghai Special Municipal Party Department's Mass Training Committee recently received a report from the Preparatory Committee of the Yarn Factory Industry Labor Union Federation stating that the East Asia Hemp Bag Factory Labor Union had been preparing for several months without any performance, leading to an order to suspend activities and dispatch personnel to investigate. The report requested filing with the committee. The committee, after receiving the report, believed that the Preparatory Committee of the Yarn Factory Industry Labor Union Federation was responsible for guiding the various labor unions in the industry and had no authority to arbitrarily suspend the activities of any labor union, let alone deal with a labor union in the industry. The nature of the East Asia Hemp Bag Factory Labor Union had nothing to do with the yarn factory industry. Therefore, it was ordered to suspend the activities of the labor union, which was a transgression of authority and disruption of the system. Therefore, yesterday, the committee instructed the Yarn Factory Industry Labor Union Federation Preparatory Committee to severely criticize and instruct the instructor, Xu Shaochuan, to provide careful guidance in the future and not to allow similar illegal and unauthorized incidents to occur again. At the same time, the committee instructed the East Asia Hemp Bag Factory Labor Union to continue preparing as usual and not to suspend activities. At the same time, in order to prevent other industrial unions from engaging in similar unauthorized actions, a circular was issued to all industry labor union preparatory committees to comply. In the future, all must adhere to their respective powers and strive to prepare without engaging in the aforementioned behavior that would lead to unauthorized and illegal charges.

Recent Tragic Locust Plague in Wugong County 140

The China Relief Society received a telegram from Ma Ri, acting on behalf of the Wugong County Relief Branch in Shaanxi, stating that the disasters in Wugong County over the years have been unprecedented and known far and wide. This year, since mid-summer, there has been a severe drought, and the rice seedlings have withered, making the autumn harvest hopeless. In the middle of last month, a large-scale locust plague broke out. At first, they only ate the leaves and branches, but then they ate the stems and ears. The seedlings are almost completely eaten, and the number of locusts is increasing without decreasing. When locusts eat rice, they hold on with their six feet, spread their four wings, and connect with each other. From a distance, the wings shine brightly like pieces of glass, boundless. Ten acres of rice can be eaten in an instant. Old and weak women and children hold poles to drive them away, weeping in the fields. The largest locusts are about eight inches long and two inches in diameter, with colors ranging from red, yellow, green, brown, and black. Their shapes are strange and frightening. They cannot be driven away, and they move like an ant colony, flying into the rice like a hurricane and rain. Human power cannot save them. It has rained twice in recent days, but the drought is too severe, so only wheat can be sown, but the locusts have not subsided. As soon as the wheat sprouts, it is eaten by the locusts. There is no harvest of early, middle, or late rice. Even the leaves of wild vegetables have been eaten. The lives of the remaining people have reached the point of desperation. The atmosphere is tragic, and the sight is unbearable. The association regards hunger and drowning as a concern and has paid special attention to the great disaster in Wuyi. It has provided two rounds of relief in the autumn of last year and this summer, and has established three disaster children shelters, saving countless lives. The merits are immeasurable, and everyone praises them. Now the locust plague is even more severe, and the human race is about to perish. Pictures of the disaster are attached, begging for rescue to complete the rescue and thorough relief effort. The people of Wu will be grateful forever. It is impossible to be urgent. The association has provided relief funds to many counties in Shaanxi in the past two years, and it has paid special attention to the relief in Wugong, using more than 100,000 yuan for emergency relief, spring relief, and seed grain. The association has also established three shelters in the disaster-stricken county, with monthly expenses of about 2,000 yuan, which are still in progress. According to reports, the locust plague will soon turn into winter relief, and it is difficult to raise relief funds if it is to be done, but the disaster victims will perish if it is not done. The association is at its wit's end and is extremely anxious, hoping that fellow countrymen at home and abroad will work together to do their best to save the situation.
